line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104681;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"><I>A*STAR’s DropArray technology has miniaturised the microtiter plate to mammoth success.</I></SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Few images evoke scientific precision quite like a lab tech hunched over a microplate, wielding a tiny, fluid-filled pipette as if to feed the world’s tiniest nestlings.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Since their invention in the 1950s, microtiter plates have become ubiquitous in life sciences labs worldwide. These rectangular sheets are moulded with tiny wells (sometimes as many as 1,536 of them), which are then filled with test fluids and used to run bioassays. Bioassays measure the quality and effects of substances, such as the effectiveness of new drugs against diseases.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Microplates are extremely versatile and can be made in a variety of materials and sizes for diverse uses. For example, samples may need to be heated or stored at extremely low temperatures, or even coated with special materials (such as gold) to conduct electricity.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Like microchips and semiconductors, microtiter plates have become the target of miniaturisation. And as with both chips and semiconductors, shrinking microplates presents a myriad of technical challenges.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">While bioassays have become automated in recent decades, even robots have difficulty handling (or, rinsing) nanoscopic samples; imagine washing a delicate porcelain tea set with a fire hose connected to a hydrant, and you get the picture.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Then there are the reagents themselves. The fluids used in bioassays are just like any other — they evaporate. The tiny volume of liquid in each well means evaporation not only happens quickly, but drastically alters the make-up of the substance, resulting in unreliable data.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Enter DropArray, a revolutionary, miniaturised microtiter plate system developed in 2008 by A*STAR’s Institute of Bioengineering and Nanotechnology (IBN).</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Smaller microplates, big gains</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">DropArray bead plates are wall-less plates that allow tiny droplets to be arranged in an array pattern. The plate’s proprietary coating is hydrophilic (water-loving) where the droplets are placed, and hydrophobic (water-repelling) in the areas between droplets. By stabilising the droplets and preventing evaporation and cross-contamination, DropArray can be easily handled and rinsed. DropArray is less than one-fifth the size of a typical microplate, and reduces the amount of reagent needed to perform bioassays by over a thousand times.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">With DropArray, researchers can now run tests that were previously out of the question. Using the conventional microtiter plate system, a significant amount of sample is required to run bioassays. This means that for some naturally scarce samples such as cancer stem cells, bioassays are virtually impossible. For instance, the testing of cancer stem cells requires a whopping 2,500 cells per well in a normal microplate – more than the amount usually present. Using DropArray, however, scientists are able to dramatically reduce the number of cells needed for screening, facilitating life-saving cancer treatment research.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Also, with less reagent needed, the costs of running lab tests are slashed by up to 90 per cent. What’s more, the time taken plummets by over 60 per cent. Hence, this miniaturisation results in everyone’s favourite outcome: cost-savings. </SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"> </SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The team that came up with DropArray took an incredibly short amount of time to develop the technology. Led by IBN scientists Prof. Jackie Y. Ying and Dr. Namyong Kim, the team overcame challenges by pooling their diverse expertise.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“We are delighted that our entrepreneurial research team of one chemist, one biologist, one biomedical engineer, one mechanical engineer and one chemical engineer took less than three years to develop a novel technology platform that would contribute significantly to reducing the cost of drug development and medication,” said Prof. Ying.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Many droplets make an ocean of change</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">As a Singaporean would say, “good things must share”. Recognising the potential of DropArray, Prof. Ying and her co-lead Dr. Kim co-founded the A*STAR spin-off company Curiox Biosystems to share this technology with biomedical researchers all over the world. Dr. Kim is the Chief Executive Officer at Curiox.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Since its inception in 2008, Curiox has sold the DropArray system to over 60 pharmaceutical companies and institutions, optimising their drug discovery and testing. Curiox has made a “major impact” in optimising bioassays for drug discovery and screening, notes Prof. Ying.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">In 2010, the company was named Asia Pacific’s Emerging Company of the Year by BioSpectrum Asia. That same year, it won several awards for outstanding technological innovation. In 2019, Curiox secured Series B funding of US$15 million, paving the way for further expansion and innovation.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Thousands of bioassays are conducted each day to analyse diseases, develop vaccines, check organ donor compatibility and more. Bioassays contribute to improved healthcare, and thanks to DropArray, the quality of these tests can only go up.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">This technology has been filed for four patent families.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#ff0000;font-size:15px;font-family:'Playfair Display';">“Our entrepreneurial research team of one chemist, one biologist, one biomedical engineer, one mechanical engineer and one chemical engineer took less than three years to develop a novel technology platform.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"><I>– Prof. Jackie Y. Ying, Founding Executive Director, Institute of Bioengineering and Nanotechnology</I></SPAN></SPAN></DIV></div>

letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The world practically runs on semiconductor chips these days in the digital age.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Unbeknownst to us, these tiny microchips power almost all our electronic devices, from televisions and laptops to even cars.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">When so much of the world’s tech runs on these microchips, it is of little surprise that the manufacturing of high-quality semiconductors is essential to keep the modern world running.. After all, you wouldn’t want your phone to break down while you’re discussing a multi-million dollar deal.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Semiconductor manufacturers have implemented rounds of rigorous testing to maintain production quality standards, one of which is wire bond inspection. This stage in the manufacturing process helps to ensure that the wire bonds are properly connected within the chips while catching any potential defects in the production line.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Over the span of two decades, wire bond inspection has been a laborious, time-consuming process that is done manually and subject to human error. This has been an immense obstacle for companies hoping to pump out microchips at a rate that befits how fast the world is consuming electronics. </SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">By tapping on pre-existing technologies and repurposing it with a new cause in mind,researchers at A*STAR’s Singapore Institute of Manufacturing Technology and local firm Component Technology have been able to revolutionise the field of wire bond inspection by making it quicker, cheaper and more efficient. </SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Science and business go hand in hand</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">In 2003, CEO and managing director of Component Technology Berne Chung saw the need for his company to innovate and expand beyond their main business. </SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The company has its roots in machinery distribution for the local semiconductor industry, but Mr Chung was ready for a change. He no longer wanted to be beholden to equipment manufacturers and in his words, “decided to take their future in their own hands.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">What Mr Chung envisioned was creating their own line of measurement and wire bonding inspection technology, which would give his company the competitive edge it needed to thrive in the global market.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">But he knew that he could not do this alone — Component Technology was a small-scale enterprise and lacked the necessary capabilities for research and development. To facilitate this, Mr Chung decided to reach out to A*STAR in 2006, sparking the collaboration with </SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">SIMTech researchers Dr. Liu Tong, Dr. Yin Xiaoming, and Dr. Li Xiang Leon, who worked tirelessly to help Mr Chung achieve the vision that he had in mind.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Months of research and hard work eventually culminated in the creation of a state-of-the-art 3D automated wire bond inspection system. The system utilises stereo vision, a technology where two cameras are placed at different angles to capture oblique images of the chip. The images are then contrasted with each other to pinpoint differences and accurately identify defects.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">It was not an easy process for the researchers. Due to the small size of the microchips, they had to contend with significant issues in the image quality, which initially led to a lower degree of accuracy than they had hoped for. However, the close working relationship with Component helped to smoothen things out. </SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“The teamwork between SIMTech and Component not only made the company’s business needs and goals clear to every team member, but also allowed the company to understand the real technical challenges we faced. It gave the team more encouragement and support,” says Dr Liu.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">While the development of stereo vision technology is not new, this was, however, one of the few times that it has been successfully applied in the semiconductor industry. With this new system in place, companies could cut their production costs by further automating the process.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Dr Liu shares about the elation the team felt when they saw that all the work they had done had finally borne fruit, “All the frustration and tiredness in the past few months was suddenly worth it. We couldn’t hide our happiness and the great sense of achievement that we felt. As a researcher, this is the most exciting moment you would experience.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">From distributor to multi-million dollar innovator</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Today, Component Technology is considered to one of the top market leaders in 3D wire-bond inspection. </SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The invention,jointly developed with SIMTech and commercialised in 2009, transformed the company from a mere distributor of semiconductor equipment to a leading innovator in the scene. The groundbreaking automated wire bond inspection system has earned Component Technology more than S$47 million in revenue and also allowed it to expand its business in the region.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">More exciting things lie ahead.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Tapping on the work they have done, the SIMTech researchers are now looking to apply this technology in creating an on-the-fly stereo vision system that will utilise three cameras instead of two for image-capturing. This promises to minimise discrepancies in measurement and further accelerate the production process, heralding a new age of automation in the field of wire bond inspection and making our electronics that much better.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">This technology has been granted two patents.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#ff0000;font-size:15px;font-family:'Playfair Display';">“The teamwork between SIMTech and Component not only made the company’s business needs and goals clear to every team member, but also allowed the company to understand the real technical challenges we faced. It gave the team more encouragement and support.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"><I>- Dr. Liu Tong, Senior Research Engineer and Section Manager (IP), Institute of Manufacturing Technology</I></SPAN></SPAN></DIV></div>

HTMLText_88DCAA1D_B967_3E77_41C6_A756F7B6662F.html = <div style="text-align:left; color:#000; "><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:20px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:20px;font-family:'Gotham Rounded Medium';"><B>Co-axial Stereo Vision for 3D Wire Bond Inspection</B></SPAN></SPAN></DIV></div>
HTMLText_88E7ACFC_B967_3BB5_41E1_1E1FA2F27E07.html = <div style="text-align:left; color:#000; "><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:25px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';">Apple Advanced</SPAN><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"><B> Chinese Input Suite</B></SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104681;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"><I>In the mid-90s, A*STAR (then the National Science and Technology Board, or NSTB) and Apple laid the foundation for today’s Mandarin speech-to-text and handwriting apps.</I></SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Before today’s voice-controlled assistants like Siri, there was Apple’s Chinese Dictation Kit (CDK). Launched in 1995, the CDK gave Mac users highly accurate Mandarin speech-to-text capabilities. It was a highly challenging task, considering that Mandarin is a complex tonal language with a very large vocabulary. The Apple Advanced Chinese Input Suite (AACIS) followed a year later, which recognised its users’ natural handwriting, even for complicated characters like 鑫 and 鬱.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">These were two world-firsts in software — large vocabulary Mandarin speech dictation for the CDK, and natural handwriting recognition in the case of the AACIS. They won high honours; the CDK bagged Singapore’s National Technology Award in 1996, while the AACIS swept the Best-of-Best Product Award in Comdex Asia.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Mr. Tng Tai Hou, who is currently A*STAR’s Deputy Director, Enterprise, along with Mr. Chow Yen-Lu, Technical Head at Apple at that time, and the combined Apple and Institute of Systems Science (Apple-ISS) team created the CDK and AACIS. They remember vividly how the project’s impossible tasks receded in the face of their team efforts.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Courting the Chinese court</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Apple was planning ahead of the coming of the internet, and it had identified China as an emerging market for its products. It noted that Singapore’s Institute of Systems Science or ISS (the predecessor to Kent Ridge Digital Labs (KRDL)) was leading in research for multilingual input. Both organisations, therefore, came together to start the Apple-ISS Research Centre in 1992.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“Both the Apple and ISS teams were driven by the need to get great user experiences for Chinese computer users via the natural style of handwriting and speech,” explains Mr. Tng, who set up the early engineering demonstrators and eventually led the development of the handwriting product.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“Singapore was still in the early stages about the role of technology and how it transforms the economy,” adds Prof. Virginia Cha, who was recruited by the Executive Director of KRDL Dr. Juzar Motiwalla in 1995 to ISS to direct the research institute’s efforts in commercialising technologies. Dr. Motiwalla was one of Singapore’s pioneering champions of technology commercialisation. Prof. Cha’s first pick for the market was language technologies. Chinese users were rapidly going online. This meant an increase in the use of Mandarin on the Internet. Concurrently, the Unicode standard, which can encode and represent every single language, was being touted by the computer science community. Globally, ISS had one of the first robust implementations of Unicode for the Unix® operating system at the time. ISS had many multilingual language research projects at the time and because there was a lack of commercial implementation of language processing, ISS developed an extensive multilingual toolkit for saving encoded scripts and symbols. With some tweaks and additions, a commercial launch for a product leveraging this would likely be successful.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">And it was groundbreaking. Contemporary reviews for the CDK hailed it “a huge hit” that deserved “critical acclaim”.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">This was after the team bootstrapped it with the in-house Large Vocabulary Speech Recognition System. Users trained the CDK by reading Mandarin to it for three hours; afterwards, the software could capture dictations in real-time.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“The Chinese Dictation Kit did not have continuous speech recognition,” Mr. Chow notes. “But it could handle millions of phrases.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">After this success with speech, handwriting was the next logical project. Compared to the English language, which is based on 26 letters in the alphabet, Mandarin has more than 15,000 characters in daily use, and limitless multi-character words. In other words, it has a huge vocabulary that prior input systems struggled with.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“So what the team in Singapore did was to invent the world’s first Chinese natural style handwriting system, and we did this by focusing entirely on data,” shares Mr. Tng. The lead researcher was Dr. Gareth Loudon, a Welshman and expert in signal processing. Not being native in Chinese, he chose the datadriven approach.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Gathering handwriting data for the team — enough to make sure the final product understood the inevitable inaccuracies when one scribbles complicated pictograms on a tablet — needed a resolute commitment to the cause.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“One of our colleagues, Ms. Goh Meng Yong, camped for two months, in the bleak winter, at the Beijing old airport,” remembers Mr. Tng, of the project team member who was pregnant at that time. “She collected over a million Chinese characters’ worth of data.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">This was an extensive dataset. With it, AACIS reliably recognised cursive Chinese handwriting. Software by many developers including Hanwang Technology, the leading software vendor for Chinese input software at that time, did not. Their system needed users to input characters one stroke at a time.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Setting the stage for Siri</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Speech recognition is now part and parcel of the platform technologies most of us are familiar with. Siri, more than Alexa and Google Voice Assistant, stands out for how it supports a Rosetta Stone’s worth of tonal languages: Cantonese, Thai, and — of course — Mandarin. This technology has been filed for one patent family and was licensed to two spin-off companies: Star+Globe Technologies and AsiaWorks.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#ff0000;font-size:15px;font-family:'Playfair Display';">“One of our colleagues camped for two months, in the bleak winter, at the Beijing old airport … She collected over a million Chinese characters’ worth of data.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"><I>– Mr. Tng Tai Hou, Deputy Director, Enterprise, A*STAR</I></SPAN></SPAN></DIV></div>

HTMLText_8AE61564_B967_CAD4_41CB_8918101DF60A.html = <div style="text-align:left; color:#000; "><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:20px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:20px;font-family:'Gotham Rounded Medium';"><B>Co-axial Stereo Vision for 3D Wire Bond Inspection</B></SPAN></SPAN></DIV></div>
HTMLText_8AED9569_B967_CADC_41E2_41790691FD09.html = <div style="text-align:left; color:#000; "><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:25px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"><B>Ultra-Low </B></SPAN><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';">Flying Height</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:25px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"><B>Femto Slider</B></SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104681;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"><I>A*STAR’s low-flying height technology enhances the capacity and performance of hard disk drives in an era of exponential data use and consumption.</I></SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Back in the 2000s, a laptop with a 40GB data storage capacity sure felt like a lot. By comparison, that’s about the same amount of storage available in today’s smartphones. In our data-driven era, we have terabyte-sized drives in our laptops, and the sheer volume of zettabytes in data that the world produces every year is mind-boggling.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The explosion in data creation and consumption is constantly fuelling demand for faster and larger-capacity data storage, necessitating more elegant technological solutions to follow suit. This global demand has been the key driver of innovative technology in data storage solutions, such as cloud computing and hard disk drives (HDDs) with higher recording density.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The persistent popularity of hard disk drives as a medium for data storage meant that specific improvements had to be made to its design to increase capacity and performance. This factor served as the inspiration behind the invention of A*STAR’s ultra low-flying height femto slider.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">In 2004, A*STAR’s ultra low-flying height femto slider successfully demonstrated that it could enhance the capacity and performance of HDDs through ultra low-flying height technology, making extremely high-density data storage possible.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">How low can you go?</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">In modern-day magnetic storage drives, the slider is the material body that supports the hard disk’s read/write drive head. Femto sliders in disk drives have come a long way, having evolved from mini sliders in the 80s to pico sliders in the 90s before finally arriving at the femto. As the names imply, sliders have evolved to become smaller over time. An airbearing femto slider is about the size of the tip of a ball point.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">In order to read and write data, the tiny slider must float over the surface of the disk while maintaining a desirable distance from the disk. To achieve higher-density data storage, sliders in hard disk drives must reach very low flying heights while maintaining flying stability over the disk. The femto slider’s air bearing design is critical to achieving flying stability over a low flying height.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">This was the challenge that the research team behind A*STAR’s femto slider had to solve. We’re talking about trying to achieve a low-flying height of a mere 2.5 nanometres while maintaining that distance with minimal flying height variation!</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Ultimately, the team had their eureka moment. Dr. Zhang Mingsheng, a Senior Scientist at A*STAR’s Institute of Materials Research and Engineering and who was previously part of the team that worked on the ultra low-flying femto slider technology at the former Data Storage Institute, compared the ground-breaking moment when they achieved a lowflying height of 2.5 nanometres to a Boeing 737 airliner maintaining a flying height of onetenth of a millimetre off the smooth ground.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“We needed not only structural mechanics and aerodynamics, but also molecular dynamics todesign the air bearing,” says Dr. Zhang when describing the biggest challenge that the team encountered during the R&amp;D process.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“The fabrication of the ultra low-flying femto slider required not only the use of traditional machining such as dicing, grinding, lapping and polishing, but also sputtering thin film deposition, photolithography and ion beam etching,” Dr. Zhang explains. In other words, these fabrication processes combined precision engineering with modern microfabrication technologies.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Aim high, fly low</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">In 2005, the team’s technological invention went on to bag the INSIC Technical Achievement Award as well as the National Technology Award. “There was a lot of trial and error, but failure is an essential part of success. We were facing it every day, but we picked ourselves up quickly and we learned from it,” Dr. Zhang recalls.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The significance of the A*STAR team’s breakthrough lies in the fact that they successfully designed and optimised femto sliders in hard disks to reach an even lower flying height than previous designs with high stability.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">By solving what was a common problem in older slider designs, the team paved the way for present-day femto sliders with higher density data storage that maximises performance. It also marks an important step towards fulfilling the ever-increasing demand for data storage capacity, which has been projected to double yearly.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“We were very happy when we achieved our target,” Dr. Zhang says, but humbly adds that for the team, this was only one milestone in the long history of the development of HDDs. “A new, higher target is still waiting ahead.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The team’s biggest takeaway from the project? “Aim high. The aim should be ambitious enough, and then take concrete steps towards that.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#ff0000;font-size:15px;font-family:'Playfair Display';">“There was a lot of trial and error, but failure is an essential part of success.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"><I>– Dr. Zhang Mingsheng, Senior Scientist, Institute of Materials Research and Engineering</I></SPAN></SPAN></DIV></div>

And no, we’re not talking about SimCity.</I></SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Like its inhabitants, a city too needs to breathe.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Urban ventilation, or the breathability of a city, is essential to the liveability of Asia’s ‘garden city’, defined by its ubiquitous lush greenery, towering skyscrapers and futuristic housing models.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Without proper planning, housing estates can turn into vertical stacks of heat-trapping, noise-amplifying concrete and metal in land-scarce Singapore.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block;
