HTMLText_97E41ACA_B967_FFDC_41C3_67A524784E24.html = <div style="text-align:left; color:#000; "><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:25px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"><B>Super </B></SPAN><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';">Wi-Fi</SPAN><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"><B> / </B></SPAN><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';">TV </SPAN><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"><B>White Space</B></SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104681;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"><I>It’s a bird, it’s a plane; no, it’s Super Wi-Fi, or more specifically, TV White Space! Despite its name, TV White Space (TVWS) has nothing to do with television, and everything to do with improving the world’s wireless connectivity.</I></SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The year is 2021: four in every five Singaporeans are part of the digital collective, and our appetite for wireless connection is forecasted to only increase in the near future. Daily life and data usage are inextricable; just glancing around quickly in a public space will show you many ‘smartphone zombies’ who are focused on their phones so much that they are oblivious to their surroundings.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">While we take for granted the constant connectivity each time we whip out our smartphones, that was not always the case in parts of the world, including Singapore’s Southern Islands.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Realising the untapped potential of TV frequencies in Singapore – its actual usage was alarmingly low at 6.5 per cent in 2012 – the A*STAR team behind TVWS sought to reimagine its usage for wireless broadband to cater to areas where conventional internet connection was not feasible.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Tapping in on old TV broadcasting frequencies to solve modern problems</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">An expert team of specialists at A*STAR comprising Dr. Oh Ser Wah, Mr. Pankaj Sharma, Ms. Chiu Ying Lay and others discovered this gap in 2012 and came up with the ingenious idea to turn frequencies that were not in use into wireless broadband. The team identified unused frequencies in the TV broadcast spectrum and breathed new life into the archaic analog broadcast technology by repurposing the old frequencies to transmit data. Raw signals picked up by TVWS antennas are then transformed into Wi-Fi frequencies that our smart phones can comprehend.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">TVWS was created as a complementary tool to reach areas inaccessible by traditional means of wireless broadband.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Their results were astounding: TVWS reaches up to ten kilometers whereas Wi-Fi only operates within 50 to 100 metres.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Fine-tuning the TVWS: the sky’s the limit</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The potential of the TVWS technology is limitless, and its significant impact in improving connectivity for rural communities in certain pockets of the Philippines and India is testimony to its capabilities. In these areas, expensive satellite technology severely limits the locals’ Internet access.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Mr. Pankaj, who comes from a rural area in India himself, elaborates, “The villagers in Philippines, Bohol didn’t have any connectivity. Even the schools, churches, municipal centres, village centres, they had no connectivity.” TVWS gave the village an affordable and quick solution for gaining access to the rest of the world.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Another project with Gardens by the Bay sought to provide guests with connectivity within its compounds. Back then, travellers’ usage of Singapore’s 3G network was expensive and restricted due to foliage that restricted line-of-sight connectivity. The team’s solution using TVWS had two benefits: firstly, it did not need line-of-sight connection and secondly, it removed the hassle of trenching the ground that the Gardens had painstakingly beautified with flora and fauna to lay down wiring cables.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The challenge, however, was getting TVWS to function within urban cityscapes due to higher rates of interference from buildings. The team’s attempts to set up a TVWS link from a high-rise rooftop in Fusionopolis to another 10 km away in Tanjong Pagar was an iterative troubleshooting process that required a trial-and-error approach. Mr. Pankaj chimes in, “It was very windy on the Fusionopolis rooftop so it was very difficult for us to mount the antenna there. We were using tripods to mount the antennas which was a bit difficult.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">A separate project that the team embarked on for GovTech which aimed to provide TVWS connectivity to six offshore Singapore islands, was also met with its own set of difficulties. Ms. Chiu recounts, “Some of the challenges we faced were not because of the TV white space, but more due to the power itself. For example, we needed solar panels when we were connecting the six islands as we had to find our own power sources. We had to adhere to the ferry schedule, else we had to stay on the island overnight.” To surmount the logistical hurdles, she developed a data-collecting system, accessible from the comfort of her home through a tap on her phone.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">However, the team concurs that solving the unique issues that came with each of their projects was part of the thrill of research and development.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Connectivity without borders</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Considered one of the leading pioneers of the TVWS technology, Singapore is the second country in the world behind the US to utilise its full potential. Apart from its usage in various industries ranging from security and healthcare to maritime, TVWS is integral to building our capabilities as a Smart Nation.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"> </SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Subsequently, Whizspace was created in 2016 by co-founders Dr. Oh and Mr. Pankaj. The local start-up has introduced TVWS to 15 other countries, providing an affordable communications solution. Their ambitious goals do not stop here: the team aspires to provide connectivity to an estimated three billion of the global population who remain unconnected.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">This technology has been filed for 10 patent families and licensed to nine companies.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#ff0000;font-size:15px;font-family:'Playfair Display';">“I came from a rural area in India and the connectivity </SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#ff0000;font-size:15px;font-family:'Playfair Display';">there was very poor, and I have seen my relatives and friends struggling to get connected. So, I thought that this technology will help me to get connectedwith them.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"><I>– Mr. Pankaj Sharma, Senior Industry Development Manager, Institute of Microelectronics</I></SPAN></SPAN></DIV></div>
HTMLText_97E48CA8_B967_FA5C_41E6_5C4A968D7BF2.html = <div style="text-align:left; color:#000; "><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:25px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"><B>Silicon Photonics</B></SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">By leveraging the speed of light to transmit data, A*STAR’s cuttingedge silicon photonics chips are the next frontier for high-performance computing systems.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Created in 1951, America’s first commercial computer, UNIVAC, weighed around 7,200 kg and could hold a mere 224 kilobytes of data. This is in stark contrast to the latest Apple MacBook Pro, which at 1.4 kg is small and light enough to be carried in our backpacks but can hold a whopping two terabytes of data.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">This trend of miniaturisation is in accordance with what is known as Moore’s Law. Intel co-founder Gordon Moore predicted in 1965 that transistors, which are used to process data, would shrink in size every two years, allowing double the number of transistors to be packed on a microchip.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Moore believed that this would lead to a dramatic increase in computing power and a drop in the relative cost of technology as microchips become smaller, faster, and more accessible to the public.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">That is, until the laws of physics caught up with this exponential growth in computing power. Transistors have become so small in recent years that we would be approaching the size of atoms if we tried to scale them down any further. This makes them increasingly impractical and costly to produce.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"> </SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Does Moore’s Law still hold true in today’s world, or have we reached the limit of miniaturisation? The answer is likely to be “More than Moore”.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Moreover, today’s high-performance systems in emerging applications of connectivity, edge AI and high-performance computing is increasingly constrained by the growing energy and communication costs associated with the huge electrical data movement between individual chips.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Let there be light</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">In order to sustain the computational power of high-performance computing systems, an efficient transfer of large amounts of data through ultra-low power, ultra-high bandwidth data links is needed. Enter Silicon Photonics (SiPh), where silicon-based microchips use photons (the basic unit of light) as a transmission and processing medium. SiPh integrated circuits (SiPh ICs) enable faster data transfer with less power consumption and heat generation than conventional electronics circuits, offering the promise of energy-efficient bandwidth scaling. SiPh ICs can be fabricated using well-established, high-volume silicon manufacturing processes. It provides a low-cost integration platform and forms the backbone for a wide range of emerging applications in high-performance computing, 5G, autonomous driving, machine learning as well as biomedical and quantum computing.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">A key figure in building up Singapore’s expertise in SiPh is A*STAR’s Prof. Dim-Lee Kwong.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Prof. Kwong, Executive Director of A*STAR’s Institute of Microelectronics (IME), has made significant contributions to Singapore’s semiconductor industry including bringing in Applied Materials, Inc. to jointly establish the US$100 million Centre of Excellence in Advanced Packaging here in 2012. Under his leadership, IME’s innovative R&amp;D foundry business model, which links semiconductor companies with local foundries to shorten the product development cycle and time-to-market for products, forged numerous partnerships between A*STAR and multinational heavyweights. Prof. Kwong received the prestigious President’s Science and Technology Medal in 2012 for his remarkable contributions to the semiconductor industry in Singapore, and he credits the honour to his team.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“We strongly believe Silicon Photonics is as pervasive as electronics, and electronicsphotonics integration through advanced packaging is essential for high-performance systems. My colleagues in IME have worked hard to build up research capabilities for the microelectronics sector,” says Prof. Kwong, “They have constantly pushed the envelope of scientific excellence and have raised the profile of Singapore’s research and development internationally.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">To Infinity... and beyond</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">What jump-started the SiPh industry in Singapore back in 2008 was the successful development of a Silicon Photonics Small Form Factor Pluggable Transceiver at IME, in collaboration with international partners.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The transceiver was revolutionary in its ability to integrate light modulation circuitry into silicon, while being fully compatible with high-volume CMOS (complementary metal oxide semiconductor) process technologies. This was a critical milestone in bringing to market a new SiPh process that met the high-speed, low-power and low-cost requirements of high-performance interconnections for computing and communications.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">As is the case with every new disruptive technology, former IME researcher Dr. Patrick Lo and the team found that companies on the ground were not entirely receptive to adopting what they had created.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“We kept pushing the device boundaries, constantly testing out the industry to refine the roadmap dynamically until the industry was ready to start considering it,” shares Dr. Lo. He trained under Prof. Kwong for his PhD and later headed IME’s nanoelectronics and photonics programme, before going on to co-found the spin-off company, Advanced Micro Foundry (AMF) in 2017. AMF is now recognised as a global leader in SiPh technology whose solutions and services can be found in data centres, telecommunications, point-of-care diagnostics systems and more.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The research team’s hard work paid off when they were awarded the President’s Technology Award in 2010.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">This technology has multiple licenses from device libraries.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV></div>

HTMLText_97FFAABF_B967_FFB4_41C9_3AC645AB549B.html = <div style="text-align:left; color:#000; "><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:20px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:20px;font-family:'Gotham Rounded Medium';"><B>Co-axial Stereo Vision for 3D Wire Bond Inspection</B></SPAN></SPAN></DIV></div>
HTMLText_A026191E_B437_8D29_41AC_5731003174B1.html = <div style="text-align:left; color:#000; "><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:25px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"><B>Adaptive Audio Streaming</B></SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:25px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"><B>Technology </B></SPAN><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';">with</SPAN><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"><B> MPEG-4 SLS</B></SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104681;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"><I>Researchers in Singapore have developed the world’s first adaptive audio streaming technology, bringing high-quality music to people wherever they go.</I></SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">"Rah, rah-ah-ah-ah, roma, roma-ma Gaga, ooh-la-la, want your bad romance.” The throbbing bass line booms in your ears as Lady Gaga’s enigmatic voice belts out a high note, sending goosebumps up your arms. If you close your eyes, you can almost imagine her performing right in front of you at a live concert.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">In reality, you are walking down the streets and grooving to your favourite pop track, which has been encoded with the innovative MPEG-4 SLS music coding technology. Matching the pristine audio quality of physical CDs while maintaining the low size of MP3 files, MPEG-4 SLS has revolutionised the music industry and rewritten the experience of listening to digital music.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Picking out the notes of MPEG-4 SLS</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Audiophiles have long lamented the inability  of digital audio formats to match up to the quality of CDs. Due to the limited storage and bandwidth available, most digital applications are unable to handle the bit rates of CD-quality music without a substantial drop in audio quality.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">To counter this problem, Professor Susanto Rahardja, Dr. Yu Rongshan, Dr. Lin Xiao and Mr. Huang Haibin, researchers from A*STAR’s Institute for Infocomm Research (I²R), sought to develop an algorithm that could compress digital audio files without compromising on the aural experience.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">What they came up with was the MPEG-4 SLS (Scalable-to-Lossless Coding), a music coding format or codec (a portmanteau of the words  “coder” and “decoder”) that is capable of compressing music files for playback without  loss in fidelity. It has more than twice the size efficiency of CDs while retaining all the original audio data during playback, unlike the lossy MP3 file format.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The codec operates on a two-layer structure — the first layer generates an AAC- (Advanced Audio Coding) compliant bit-stream, which allows high-fidelity audio to be played at a normal bit rate while the second Lossless Enhanced (LLE) layer allows files to be pre-encoded at varying bit rates. This means that our music streaming experience will remain consistent even if our mobile connection suddenly drops — if we are in the depths of Singapore’s Bras Basah MRT station, for example — as the codec is able to intelligently reduce the bit rate to accommodate the drop in Internet bandwidth. With this feature, music lovers can experience high-quality music wherever they go without being confined to deskbound hi-fi stereo systems.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The journey to developing MPEG-4 SLS, however, was not as smooth as a jazz track. Even though the team’s codec had surpassed many of their competitors’ during the five year-long standardisation phase — a period of performance testing before the product can be internationally standardized — they encountered many frightening moments half-way through the developmental process. At one point, the team learned that a larger, competing organisation’s algorithm had outperformed theirs. Prof. Rahardja recalls, “Our technology was threatened to the point that it could completely be wiped out even though prior to this we had won many competitions in the same standardisation.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Instead of feeling daunted, Prof. Rahardja and his team buckled down to improve their codec even further. Describing this process as “a continuous cycle of research” rather than “a one-time effort”, their assiduity eventually paid off.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">In 2006, the MPEG-4 SLS codec was adopted as a global standard by the International Standard Organisation. This feat was all the more impressive as the team had emerged triumphant in a highly competitive field dominated by larger, multinational players in the audio industry. Prof. Rahardja’s team first won the Tan Kah Kee Young Inventor’s Award (GOLD) Open Section in 2003. They went on to clinch the National Technology Award in 2007 for their contributions to the advancement of digital audio coding technologies and the adoption of the MPEG-4 SLS codec as an international standard for audio compression.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“Every moment of doing this project is exciting and we would need to continuously upgrade the technology and defend it against replacement,” Prof. Rahardja says, “such that at the end of the standardisation, the patented technology can be adopted and internationally standardised.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Beats that go on and on</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">When the MPEG-4 SLS codec was launched, Mr. Philip Lim, then Chief Executive Officer of Exploit Technologies, A*STAR’s commercialisation arm which has been renamed Enterprise, believed that “this innovative adaptive technology could completely change the digital music industry, just as the introduction of MP3 did many years ago”.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">In 2010, the MPEG-4 SLS became the world’s first Adaptive Audio Streaming technology, as it was adopted by the industry to cater to a growing consumer base that craved instantaneous, high-quality music streaming. Now, 14 years since its inception, MPEG-4 SLS is still widely used around the world, and it has redefined the global standards of high-quality music streaming over the past decade. Its legacy is a testament to I²R’s efforts in improving the competitiveness of Singapore’s infocomm and media sectors.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Each time we open Spotify and listen to a jazz vocal by Billie Holiday, an overture performed by the London Symphony Orchestra or a ballad by Stefanie Sun, we are not just bathing in their music; if we close our eyes and listen carefully, we can also hear the echoes still emanating from this innovation. This technology has been filed for 14 patent families.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#ff0000;font-size:15px;font-family:'Playfair Display';">“Every moment of doing this project is exciting and we would need to continuously upgrade the technology, defend it against replacement, such that at the end of the standardisation, the patented technology can be adopted and internationally standardised.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"><I>– Prof. Susanto Rahardja, former Deputy Executive Director (Research) at the Institute for Infocomm Research</I></SPAN></SPAN></DIV></div>
HTMLText_A02EC919_B437_8D2B_41C9_7FFEA40C0386.html = <div style="text-align:left; color:#000; "><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:20px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:20px;font-family:'Gotham Rounded Medium';"><B>Co-axial Stereo Vision for 3D Wire Bond Inspection</B></SPAN></SPAN></DIV></div>
HTMLText_A2555DE3_BC6A_BBFE_41DD_A0A430C61F3C.html = <div style="text-align:left; color:#000; "><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:25px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"><B>CoVsurver: </B></SPAN><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';">Virus Surveillance Platform</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">When the COVID-19 pandemic hit, an urgent need emerged for a tool that would allow us to understand what the virus was, when it was mutating, and how. CoVsurver, a computational surveillance tool that tracks COVID-19 variants and mutations through the global data science platform GISAID was A*STAR’s answer.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">From development of life-saving drugs for HIV patients, to the eradication of the once virulent and deadly smallpox, history has shown us that medical intervention can transform life-threatening illnesses into milder inconveniences. But this isn’t sorcery — the magic ingredient is knowledge.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Computational surveillance and analysis tools for viruses play an increasingly important role in guiding research and medical interventions. These tools help scientists to interpret viral genomes (the complete set of their genetic code) and identify important mutations. Pinpointing and understanding these mutations is key as mutations can escalate the threat viruses pose to our communities. Mutations may arm viruses with new capabilities such as drug resistance, increased virulence and heightened infectivity.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">These tools become much more powerful when used in conjunction with real-time data (which is only possible if people around the world share willingly and rapidly). The GISAID (Global Initiative on Sharing All Influenza Data) data science initiative, founded in 2006, fits the bill perfectly with a unique sharing mechanism which provides open access to data to researchers who identify themselves and uphold scientific etiquette by acknowledging the data source, while respecting the data owners’ rights and interests. This incentivises rapid sharing, and thus has become the backbone of the World Health Organisation’s (WHO) global influenza surveillance programme for vaccine selection and drug resistance tracking.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">From fighting flus to the front lines of the pandemic</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">A*STAR’s Bioinformatics Institute (BII) has been collaborating with GISAID since the 2009 H1N1 pandemic. It provided a tool called FluSurver that was used by WHO and other national centres to detect drug-resistant strains. This paved the way for fruitful collaborations over a decade, which intensified in the next devastating pandemic.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">When COVID-19 began to spread swiftly across the globe in 2020, the novelty of the disease only amplified its threat. The world needed to know more to effectively fight it. To fill these gaps in information about the virus, the team at BII devoted themselves to creating a surveillance tool to track the novel virus. CoVsurver, the product of their hard work, would quickly become indispensable in the global public health response.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">CoVsurver was a creation of necessity, built upon the well laid foundation of the FluSurver. Despite the strong start, BII scientists Dr. Sebastian Maurer-Stroh and Mr. Raphael Lee and their team soon met an unprecedented problem.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Managing the (data) waves of a global pandemic</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">From the start of their project, the CoVsurver team was faced with a daunting challenge: an immense amount of data that needed to be received, sorted through, and analysed. “With the coronavirus pandemic, it started with 100 sequences per week, then 100 sequences per day, then 1,000 sequences per day, then 20,000 sequences per day,” Dr. Maurer-Stroh tells us.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">These exponentially growing numbers were accompanied by climbing pressures as the pandemic began to take its toll across the world. FluSurver, designed to handle just 20,000 genomes per year for influenza, was not quite up to the task. Although the framework FluSurver provided was a definite boon, the team had to adapt the technology and create something new.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">In the race to develop CoVsurver in a compressed timeline, the team devoted their time to poring over scientific literature and harmonising vast databases. With a host of tasks to juggle and time of the utmost essence in the initial stages of development, they worked tirelessly and slept little.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">By February 2020, the team had put together a programme that could rapidly analyse COVID-19 data to identify differences, or mutations, in new genomes submitted. In the months that followed, they worked to streamline the tool, whittling down the time taken to generate a report and increasing its data handling capacity. Over an astoundingly short period of time, they managed to bring CoVsurver from an ambitious goal to a game-changing reality.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Making a mark on the global stage</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">GISAID with CoVsurver as an underlying annotation pipeline has accelerated our understanding of the novel coronavirus at critical moments in the battle against COVID-19. It quickly became the primary source of genomic and associated data from SARS-CoV-2 cases. This meant that CoVsurver enabled the GISAID platform and the global scientific community to understand how the virus was changing as it spread and where these changes were occurring in its RNA and 3D structure. This information was vital in the development of diagnostic tests, therapeutics, and vaccines, that have helped get the pandemic under control.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Although there is much to be said of CoVsurver as a technical feat, its success is not only a story of technological advancement. Instead, it is one of history and its continuity, and more than that, of the people that make it happen. Mr. Lee tells us that to realise momentous projects like this, “We need to dream a lot, have vision, passion, work hard, dedication, a right team with a great leader, have users who help us spread the word, and seize the right opportunities with great timing.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#ff0000;font-size:15px;font-family:'Playfair Display';">“Several factors are needed for the success of this project. We need to dream a lot, have vision, passion, work hard, dedication, a right team with a great leader, have users who help us spread the word, seizing the right opportunity and great timing.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"><I>– Mr. Raphael Lee, Research Manager, Bioinformatics Institute</I></SPAN></SPAN></DIV></div>
