HTMLText_A63673AE_B73C_CE55_41E2_CD14E852054A.html = <div style="text-align:left; color:#000; "><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:25px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"><B>GUSTO: </B></SPAN><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';">Growing Up Towards</SPAN><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"><B> Healthy Outcomes in Singapore</B></SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104681;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"><I>Growing up in Singapore Towards Healthy Outcomes (GUSTO) is a birth cohort study of 1,000 mother-child pairs. GUSTO analyses the effects of maternal mental and physical health during pregnancy on the child’s health and development after birth. The findings on gestational diabetes have led to policy changes and better care for expectant mothers.</I></SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">One in five of all pregnancies in Singapore is complicated by gestational diabetes, but did you know that before 2015, it was assumed to be far less prevalent? Gestational diabetes is a condition where an expectant mother develops high blood glucose levels during the physiological changes associated with pregnancy. This is because hormones produced by the placenta during pregnancy cause the mother’s body cells to become more resistant to insulin. As insulin is used by the body to transport blood glucose into cells for energy production, insulin resistance results in high blood glucose levels and is often a precursor to diabetes.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Despite its prevalence, gestational diabetes was woefully underdiagnosed pre-2015 as only expectant mothers who were perceived to be at high risk for the condition were screened. That was until GUSTO (Growing up in Singapore Towards Healthy Outcomes), a longitudinal birth cohort study of children and their mothers – beginning from pregnancy– demonstrated how the health, diet and lifestyle of expectant mothers influences their children’s growth. GUSTO, started in 2008, is a collaborative effort involving the National University Health System (NUHS), KK Women’s and Children’s Hospital (KKH) and A*STAR’s Singapore Institute of Clinical Sciences (SICS).</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">As a result of the GUSTO study findings in 2015, now all expectant mothers in Singapore undergo “universal screening”, and are recommended to be tested for diabetes after week 24 of their pregnancy to better manage the condition and outcomes. Gestational diabetes is a known major risk factor for a mother’s child to develop conditions such as obesity and diabetes later on in life, hence early diagnosis and awareness are important.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">A couple’s row over breastfeeding and how it led to policy change</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">One would hardly fathom that a marital disagreement could be the seed for a scientific study, but for Prof. Chong Yap Seng, Chief Clinical Officer of SICS and Dean of the NUS Yong Loo Lin School of Medicine, getting thrown out of the room by his wife kick-started the research idea that would lead to GUSTO.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">After the birth of their first child in 1999, Prof. Chong, an obstetrician, questioned his wife’s decision to persist with the challenges of breastfeeding their firstborn instead of opting for the free infant formula given out by hospitals. His wife was unimpressed, and Prof. Chong found himself trying to prove whether she was right that breast is best. It turned out that she was, and he began to develop an interest in early childhood nutrition.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">However, it was not until 2006 that GUSTO began to take shape. An exchange agreement saw former Chief Science Advisor to the Prime Minister of New Zealand, Prof. Sir Peter Gluckman, giving a lecture at the KHH on how health and disease develop Gluckman’s idea of pregnancy programming a child called out to Prof. Chong, and the two went out for dinner. Sparks flew between the pair as they discovered that Prof. Chong’s work on breastfeeding and early nutrition complemented Prof. Sir Gluckman’s interests in pregnancy and the programming of a child. This led to further discussions and culminated in their historic collaboration two years later as a longitudinal birth cohort study, i.e. GUSTO. The project was supported by a S$25 million Translational Clinical Research Flagship Programme Grant from the National Medical Research Council (NMRC), the biggest funding offered at that time in Singapore.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">In June 2009, 1,200 GUSTO subjects were recruited. Prof. Chong and his team had initially thought of a 100,000-strong cohort but realised that Singapore simply did not have the numbers. They reduced this to 10,000, and soon decided on an in-depth study conducted on a smaller number of participants. Among other tests, maternal blood sampling and Oral Glucose Tolerance Tests (OGTTs) were done during pregnancy to detect diabetes. The OGTT looks at whether a patient’s body can process sugar effectively. It is administered via a glucose drink after an eight-to-12-hour fast. Prior to downing the drink, the patient’s blood glucose level is measured. After taking the drink, blood samples are collected at regular 30-60-minute intervals for up to three hours. Blood glucose levels are then measured to determine whether a patient is diabetic.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The OGTTs conducted on the GUSTO mothers produced a result that the team did not expect. Instead of the projected five to ten per cent prevalence of gestational diabetes, they found 20 per cent of expectant mothers to be afflicted with the condition.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“Not only is the incidence of gestational diabetes double of what we thought it wouldbe — one in five women will have GDM — and almost half of these women with GDM will go on to become diabetic within the next five years,” Prof. Chong says.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">He presented these findings in 2015. Within three years, a policy change resulted in diabetes screening for all expectant mothers in Singapore.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Programming pregnancies for better life outcomes</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Beyond gestational diabetes, GUSTO also analyses the effects of various other maternal health markers on children. As the children involved in GUSTO approach adolescence, Prof. Chong and his team are curious to see how they continue developing, even in their later years — following the GUSTO cohort through life will provide invaluable insights into their brain development, health and lifespan, and potentially further influence policy making.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">While the results have led to real-world change, a study of such reach required stamina and persistence from Prof. Chong’s team, as well as cooperation and continued support from the participants.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“We had about 1,130 babies delivered in GUSTO, and as of today we are probably still in contact with about 1,000 children and seeing them on a regular basis,” Prof. Chong says. In December 2018, the team even held a tenth anniversary event involving the participants. “It was great to see the GUSTO kids playing and happy to be there; you could see the families were happy to be part of the larger GUSTO family.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">They may not have realised the contribution they were about to make when they signed up for the study in 2008. However, by giving hours of their time over more than ten years, the GUSTO cohort has helped Prof. Chong and his team push for better preventive healthcare in Singapore. By showing how maternal health affects the growth and development of the child, GUSTO has paved the way for improving the health and quality of life for unborn children worldwide. As the GUSTO children grow up, observations of their health and development may lead to further discoveries on how early nutrition affects people through their lives; it may also help governments implement more effective healthcare policies to improve the health of their citizens.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV></div>
HTMLText_A636C3AF_B73C_CE53_41C8_3BC64F92C062.html = <div style="text-align:left; color:#000; "><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:20px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:20px;font-family:'Gotham Rounded Medium';"><B>Co-axial Stereo Vision for 3D Wire Bond Inspection</B></SPAN></SPAN></DIV></div>
HTMLText_A63713A6_B73C_CE55_41C4_BD13AA225FD0.html = <div style="text-align:left; color:#000; "><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:25px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"><B>Digital Pathology </B></SPAN><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';">Using an</SPAN><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"><B> Adaptive Algorithm</B></SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104681;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"><I>Casting a laser beam at different types of media causes them to emit different coloured signals. This concept, known as second-harmonic imaging, is revolutionising liver disease diagnostics globally.</I></SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Plopping on the couch with a box of fried chicken while binge-watching Netflix seems like the go-to way to de-stress after a long day at work or school. But our sedentary habits have ramifications both for ourselves and our healthcare system. According to a World Health Organisation study on adolescents from 2001 to 2016, three-quarters of Singaporean teens did not meet the recommended guidelines of at least one-hour of physical activity daily.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Our poor dietary habits and sedentary lifestyles over the years correlate with climbing cases of liver disease, such as liver fibrosis, in Singapore. Hence, the need for swift diagnostics has never been more pressing. Thankfully, Prof. Hanry Yu, Senior Principal Investigator at A*STAR’s Institute of Bioengineering and Bioimaging (IBB), saw the potential for non-linear optical imaging to revolutionise medical diagnostics, vastly simplifying what was once a convoluted process.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Shedding light on liver fibrosis</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Liver fibrosis is the scarring of liver tissue due to the accumulation of proteins such as collagen. There are multiple causes, such as poor diet, physical inactivity, obesity and alcohol abuse. As the disease progresses, the liver’s ability to process various nutrients, drugs and toxins gradually declines. Without intervention, continued development of fibrosis eventually leads to cirrhosis, an often painful and life-threatening condition whereby the liver loses its ability to function.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Traditionally, liver fibrosis is detected through the presence of collagen fibres in liver cells collected through biopsies. This involves a time-consuming, manual staining process to colour the collagen so that they are visible under the microscope.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Second-harmonic generation (SHG) micro-scopy eliminates the need for staining as laser beams directed at the samples — in this case, collagen fibres in liver tissue — combine to form a new beam half the wavelength of the original beams. This resultant beam produces an SHG signal of a different colour, allowing it to be picked up easily with a special optical microscope. Thus, even small amounts of collagen fibres can be illuminated, enabling doctors to diagnose patients quickly and accurately. Furthermore, bypassing the staining process saves precious time in Singapore’s healthcare industry.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Illuminating the shadows</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">SHG imaging has been around for quite a long time in the world of academic physics. Prof. Yu wondered if he could harness that technology and apply it into the field of bioengineering. It was not an easy process.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">It was the early 2000s, and microscope building was not exactly a walk in the park. In a world of rigid scientific classification and categorisation, Prof. Yu also found his idea of marrying applied physics with clinical science unappreciated.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“Clinical journals found our work too technical and technical journals found it too medical and not technically novel,” he says. This frustrating mutual exclusivity of the different scientific fields extended to his manpower search. “In those days, people with interdisciplinary mindsets were hard to find and recruit. People only wanted to publish papers without desiring for translational and commercial outputs.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Undeterred, Prof. Yu charted his own path by incorporating theory into real-world play. He built the infrastructure for an SHG microscope at the Institute of Bioengineering and Nanotechnology (IBN) funded by A*STAR, and when the Singapore-MIT Alliance trained PhD students to work with IBN staff on liver fibrosis research in 2005, he was ready.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">After the initial uphill battle, the R&amp;D process returned many exciting and rewarding moments. Prof Yu and his team confirmed that liver biopsy samples with very minute amounts of collagen fibres could be visualised using SHG technology. Discovering that quantification of collagen fibres generated stronger signals in liver fibrosis samples than normal liver samples served as affirmation of the technology. Based on these findings, Prof. Yu and his team then developed a semi-automated (which was later improved to a fully automated) quantification method, enabling liver biopsy samples to be examined and analysed digitally via an artificial intelligence (AI) system.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Seeing liver disease diagnostics in a new light</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">In April 2010, Prof. Yu’s hard work to bring research to everyday applications came to fruition. A*STAR spin-off MedTech company HistoIndex was established with Prof. Yu as the Founding Scientist. The firm specialises in AI-based stain-free digital pathology solutions. Now, efficient and accurate SHG-enabled testing is available for liver diseases via clinical trials. Globally, more than 150 hospitals, universities, research institutes, CROs and drug development companies have benefited from Prof Yu’s vision. A 2019 study arising from a collaboration between HistoIndex and Singapore General Hospital demonstrated the high accuracy of AI-assisted detection and counting of fatty liver cells using SHG microscopy.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">This bodes well for ongoing clinical trials and for the future of liver disease diagnostics.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Singaporeans know well that efficiency is the name of the game. This cannot be more relevant than in the healthcare industry, where the speed of diagnosis and treatment may well be a matter of life or death. With the help of AI technology, SHG microscopy is contributing to the world of pathology by streamlining the liver disease diagnosis process. With liver disease in Singapore poised to rise alongside increasing modern comforts, this could potentially save lives and reduce the number of patients requiring serious medical interventions, such as liver transplants. That said, maybe it’s high time for us to reflect on our couch potato habits too.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">This technology has been filed for four patent families and licensed to two companies.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#ff0000;font-size:15px;font-family:'Playfair Display';">“Clinical journals found our work too technical and technical journals found it too medical and not technically novel ... People only wanted to publish papers without desiring for translational and commercial outputs.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"><I>– Prof. Hanry Yu, Senior Principal Investigator, Institute of Bioengineering and Bioimaging</I></SPAN></SPAN></DIV></div>

HTMLText_A63F036F_B73C_CED3_41DC_0B81A74D4A36.html = <div style="text-align:left; color:#000; "><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:25px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"><B>Anti-Viral </B></SPAN><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';">and</SPAN><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"><B> Anti-Bacterial Coating </B></SPAN><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';">Inspired by</SPAN><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"><B> Dragonfly Wings</B></SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104681;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"><I>Microscopic spikes are the secret weapon of dragonflies and cicadas against millions of potentially life-threatening microbes in their environments. Now, A*STAR scientists are harnessing this concept to protect us from transmissible diseases in public spaces.</I></SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">We think of the wings of dragonflies and cicadas as delicate things. Shiny, intricate, gossamer-like. But a look through a microscope reveals a different story. On a microscopic level, we would see that in actuality, these translucent wings are armed with rows of sharp spikes</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">called nanopillars.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">They stand ready to impale nature’s most abundant threats: pathogens. These surfaces prove to be highly effective weapons against dangerous microbes, ripping through their defences and killing them upon contact.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Harnessing nature’s weapons</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Now, scientists at A*STAR’s Institute of Bioengineering and Bioimaging (IBB) have found a way to harness the ingenious, natural technology these insects carry on their wings to keep us safer in public spaces. In the current COVID-19 climate, anxiety about the cleanliness of high contact surfaces has risen to the surface of public consciousnesses. We are right to be worried: 80 per cent of common infections are spread by hands. More than ever, we are watching where we go and what we touch.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">For Senior Principal Investigator Dr. Yugen Zhang and his team, this issue has been on their mind for years. Their invention, an antiviral and antibacterial coating that seems to be the perfect weapon in a pandemic, has been years in the making. Yet, for them, the road to gaining the public’sinterest and commercial success was not always clear.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Initiated before 2019, the initial aim of the project was to address a major issue associated with sterilisation agents. “The original intention was to generate materials that had a novel antibacterial and antifungal mechanism, without the development of multidrug resistance,” Dr. Zhang tells us.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">In other words, the team wanted to combat the risks of breeding stronger germs with the use of conventional chemical disinfectants. Disinfectants are not 100 per cent effective, meaning they leave a very small population of germs alive. These remaining germs, carrying random mutations that allow them to better evade disinfectants’ chemical attacks, can then reproduce in exponential numbers, unhindered by competition from weaker germ strains.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Over time, bacteria and fungi can accumulate these evasive mutations, giving rise to superbugs that are resistant to the chemical attacks of all existing conventional disinfectants.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The structural attack mounted by the nanopillars in Dr. Zhang and his team’s novel solution circumvents this risk. As these nanopillars are small enough to pierce through the cell membranes of microbes, they reliably eliminate pathogens mechanically without accelerating the development of superbugs.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Alongside this, Dr. Zhang had a vision that his material could address environmental concerns. While we mostly think of disinfectants as a highly effective eliminator of bacterial life, germs are not the only organisms they threaten. Conventional disinfectants contain a cocktail of chemicals that can be toxic to plant and animal life.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">As urban life increasingly encroaches upon wild spaces, we are bearing witness to rising instances of wildlife coming into contact with, and being poisoned, by these substances. When this happens, effects can ripple through food chains as poisons accumulate in the bodies of organisms in direct contact with toxins and their predators. This could eventually lead to widespread animal and plant death, and devastating consequences for the ecosystems they inhabit.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">By moving away from a reliance on potentially dangerous chemicals used in conventional disinfectants, the dragonfly-inspired coating could help us protect precious plant and animal lives alongside our own.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Evolving technology for evolving circumstances</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Though one of the team’s major initial challenges was in creating awareness of their technology and convincing industries and end users to adopt their coating, the rapidly accelerating global pandemic would make their invention extremely relevant.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">When the COVID-19 pandemic hit, Dr. Zhang and his team were hopeful that their materials could aid in the fight against the disease. To their disappointment, however, technology based on the first generation of their materials was unable to kill the COVID-19 virus. But to them, this was only a setback. “This then spurred us on to finetune and modify our materials to further improve their performance against viruses,” says Dr. Zhang.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Eventually, not only did they succeed in creating a coating that effectively eliminated the COVID-19 virus, they also discovered an exciting new ability in their invention. To Dr. Zhang’s surprise, “We found that some of our synthesized nanopillar surfaces were able to kill both bacteria cells that were attached to the surfaces and those that were not.” This meant that the coating was able to kill even free-floating germs that were not in contact with it.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">This was not a capability observed in natural nanopillars and the team was excited to learn that they had augmented the capacity of this natural structure. They now not only had nanostructured surfaces, but also nanostructured particles whose effectiveness did not rely on bacteria attaching to a surface. This meant that their technology could more efficiently and reliably kill microbes, making their technology more powerful and more flexible. With this new discovery, the team could imagine even greater possibilities for their technology.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Watching their project take flight</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The team’s continued efforts have come into fruition in high-impact, commercially successful products. It’s easy to see why: their technology is scalable, environmentally friendly, and its capabilities are in high demand.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">They have launched two spin-off companies from technologies developed in the project and applied their discoveries to antiviral masks and antiviral coatings to prevent COVID-19 transmission. These have immense transformative potential, particularly in sterile environments like hospitals and clinics. Beyond this, the team is continuing to explore ways to adapt their ideas to an ever-growing range of applications.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The dragonfly-inspired coating has already made its mark in the fight against the COVID- 19 pandemic. But with governments and businesses already asking themselves what they can do to prepare themselves for the threat of the next pandemic, its work may only have just begun.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">This technology has been filed for four patent families.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#ff0000;font-size:15px;font-family:'Playfair Display';">“The teamwork between SIMTech and Component not only made the company’s business needs and goals clear to every team member, but also allowed the company to understand the real technical challenges we faced. It gave the team more encouragement and support.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"><I>- Dr. Liu Tong, Senior Research Engineer and Section Manager (IP), Institute of Manufacturing Technology</I></SPAN></SPAN></DIV></div>

white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104681;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"><I>A*STAR’s Institute of High Performance Computing and Sembcorp Marine jointly developed a system that treats water with energy-efficient ultraviolet light, making an environmentally sustainable improvement to international shipping.</I></SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0;
