white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The folktales of the Southeast Asian archipelago reflect our long understanding that a healthy ocean means thriving trade. Sang Nila Utama discovered Singapore when, with his crown, he calmed a tsunami in the Straits. Mai An Tiêm introduced watermelons to Vietnam by bartering them with passing ships when he was exiled to a deserted island shore.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">In contemporary times, over 90 per cent of international trade goods are transported by ships. This maritime trade discharges tons of ballast water during each trip — this torrent of untreated water releases bacterial pathogens into the marine ecosystem.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Spurred by this need for maritime trade responsibility, Dr. Li Hongying, Senior Scientist at A*STAR’s Institute of High Performance Computing (IHPC), and her team jointly captained the development of a new, greener ballast water treatment system with Sembcorp Marine. The design of their system, Semb-Eco LUV, was supported by computational calculations. It is non-chemical and byproduct-free, translates to a more sustainable marine ecosystem through environmental protection.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">One man’s water is another’s waste</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The Semb-Eco LUV is the world’s first Ultra- Low Frequency ultraviolet (UV) light ballast water management system (BWMS). It is the first (and currently the only) such system to pass usability testing in challenging tropical water conditions.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Ballast water is needed by all ships. Making up about half the initial multi-ton cargo load, ballast water is typically stored all over the ship to improved maneuverability and provide stability for different legs of the journey. Without the right amount of ballast water, ships may be more vulnerable to wind conditions, and encounter difficulties propelling as a result of incompletely submerged propellers.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">So, a ship’s crew always makes sure to fill the tanks before they leave the port. On the voyage, they release the tank valves as needed. All the faster to reach the next port with.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">However, water from port A — let’s say Tortuga—naturally causes ecological harm when dropped elsewhere — let’s say the Singapore Straits.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">There are 7,000 species transferred species. “Ballast water contains a variety of biological in ballast water hourly and 10 billion tons of ballast water transported annually,” says Dr. Li. “If the ballast water is discharged into the ocean without treatment, it would potentially introduce invasive species, and pollute the marine environment leading to an ecosystem disaster.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">UV light is the traditional remedy here. Ideally, bacteria capable of producing pollutants absorb its energy, which prevents them from replicating their genetic codes. As a result, there is neither formation of pollution nor harmful by-products.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">But a 2020 test by Korean researchers found that BWMSs approved by the International Maritime Organisation (IMO) can fail in tropical waters, where many solid particles turn up at estuaries. Here, UV light works less effectively.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“The results demonstrate,” the researchers write, “that there is a significant gap between the technology currently available and capacity to meet IMO and US Coast Guard (USCG) standards.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Dr. Li’s innovation worked towards maximum sustainability with these two key industry standards in mind. Her team developed a new Computational Fluid Dynamics (CFD) framework for BWMS performance and performed rigorous practical numerical trials with the number and positions of the UV lamps.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“We found a design which performs better than the previous one, and yet is more energy- efficient,” says Dr. Li. “That was the most exciting moment.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">With an auto back-flush filter, it operates well in tropical waters. And mid-to-large-scale models, like the team’s LBW-240, consume less power and have a smaller ecological footprint than existing in the market.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Bringing Semb-Eco LUV to market required sailing into strange tides. The team was bombarded with 10 rounds of questions before product certification.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“The whole journey lasted more than one year,” shares Dr. Li. “Our rebuttal is even thicker than a PhD thesis.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The IHPC researchers hunkered down with Sembcorp Marine’s R&amp;D team to address the technical questions. The result: Semb-Eco LUV, in an era where its competing peers have failed, is today certified by both the IMO and the Coast Guard.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">A sea-change into viral strains</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Development insights from the Semb-Eco LUV project are being repurposed to fight the COVID-19 pandemic.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“We are collaborating with sister research institutes and companies to design an Ultraviolet-C LED product to inactivate the SARS-CoV-2 virus in air,” says Dr. Li.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The team’s biggest takeaway from this BWMS project, it turns out, was the capability to model bacterial movement in fluids. This is useful for studying disinfection of airborne droplets, a common transmission mode for respiratory viruses. Hence, their impetus for machines which mitigate the airborne transmission risk of COVID-19.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">All this research means two different interventions for two pressing problems. The oceans are endless and the air is ethereal — and the IHPC team is becoming great guardians of both.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#ff0000;font-size:15px;font-family:'Playfair Display';">“The most excitingmoment was when we found a design which performs better than the previous one, and yet is more energy-efficient.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"><I>– Dr. Li Hongying, Senior Scientist, Institute of High Performance Computing</I></SPAN></SPAN></DIV></div>
HTMLText_A8077CA3_BC2B_987E_41C8_96E8F7BE3E0D.html = <div style="text-align:left; color:#000; "><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:20px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:20px;font-family:'Gotham Rounded Medium';"><B>Co-axial Stereo Vision for 3D Wire Bond Inspection</B></SPAN></SPAN></DIV></div>
HTMLText_A80FDCA7_BC2B_9846_41E4_0679D62C06DB.html = <div style="text-align:left; color:#000; "><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:25px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"><B>Vitreogel</B></SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104681;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"><I>Vitreogel is a new biomaterial that turns from a liquid into a gel when it reaches normal body temperature (37°C). It is a huge improvement over prior treatment options and promises to greatly improve the postsurgery experience of patients suffering from retinal detachment.</I></SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">If you have ever wondered why our eyeballs are, well, balls, you would have the vitreous humour to thank. It is the jelly-like substance that partly constitutes the whites of our eyes and gives our eyeballs their spherical shape. For most of our lives, the vitreous humour resides happily between the lenses at the front of our eyes and our retinas at the back.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Over time, however, the viscous vitreous can degrade and even liquify, causing a vision-threatening condition called retinal detachment. Addressing this condition often involves a surgery called a vitrectomy, in which the eye must be drained of the vitreous humour to allow the repair of the retina.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Once the surgical repair is complete, the patient’s eye is refilled. This is currently done with expansile gases or silicone oils. But these are temporary substitutes with difficult-to-manage limitations. Expansile gases force patients to spend their days and nights in a face-down position for weeks, while silicone oils can put patients at risk of many complications, including glaucoma, retinal toxicity and corneal decompensation.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Changing the state of patient care</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">With Vitreogel, however, Professor Loh Xian Jun and his team — hailing from institutions like A*STAR’s Institute of Materials Research and Engineering (IMRE) and Institute of Molecular and Cell Biology (IMCB), and the National University of Singapore — have changed patients’ recovery prospects.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Vitreogel is actually the vitreous substitute of a thermogel. A thermogel is made of over 90 per cent water, much like the vitreous it is designed to replace. The team developed and used EPC Poly (PEG/PPG/PCL urethane)s, a polymer which consists of polycaprolactone (PCL), polyethylene glycol (PEG) and polypropylene glycol (PPG), to make up the remaining composition of the gel. This polymer component allows Vitreogel to miraculously and spontaneously transform from a liquid to a clear gel once injected into the human eye.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Because it so closely mimics an original vitreous in surface tension and consistency, Vitreogel radically simplifies the measures patients must take during their recovery phases. Gone are the mandatory awkward postures and worries about complications. Instead, patients can go about their daily lives with minimal disruption, since Vitreogel allows them to see clearly and move about normally.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Additionally, unlike silicone oils, it breaks down on its own over time, which not only mitigates the need for a removal surgery, but also supports the body in replacing its own vitreous within three months of the operation.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Behind this innovation was the stubborn resilience of a team of driven scientists. Thinking about how water changes states as it is heated or frozen, Prof. Loh was struck by an exciting new idea: a biocompatible material that would do the opposite — change its form from a liquid to a solid in reaction to heat. Such a material would have to be initially liquid in order to be injected, but subsequently be able to solidify and take on the structure and function of the vitreous of the human eye once it is exposed to heat.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">If they could develop a version of this material that was reliable and non-toxic, it could prove transformative for patients recovering from retinal operations. Driven by this goal to improve patient care and experience, Prof. Loh and his team set out to develop this ambitious material. To ensure that it was medically viable, they decided to collaborate with clinician-scientist Dr. Su Xinyi from IMCB, who provided the medical know-how.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">For the team, the formula for this imagined gel was elusive in the early days of their research. On some days, the prototype solution they produced puddled and refused to budge from its liquid state. On other days, it stubbornly refused to drop its rigid form. Even when they managed to coax it into changing states, there was still the matter of ensuring that this happened exactly at 37°C, which is the normal temperature of the human body.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Their frustration was compounded by how difficult it was to even identify what exactly was causing problems in their prototype gels. Prof. Loh remarks, “There were many parameters I had to tweak, but I only knew about the variable… when the material failed to gel.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The moment they found the winning formula was almost indescribable for Prof. Loh. He recalls, “I still remembered the moment when it gelled up, even though the process was in the matter of seconds, it felt like time stood still for a moment and I watched the liquid solution almost magically transform into a solid gel.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Solidifying its place as a medical innovation</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">After about nine months of rigorous testing and tweaking, Vitreogel is almost ready for clinical trials, which made Prof. Loh feel “proud, happy, and a quiet sense of satisfaction”. Their work was going to bring some much-needed relief to patients.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">With the successful development of Vitreogel under their belts, the team is now exploring the many possible uses for the material’s unique properties. With its potential as a protective material or even a controlled delivery platform for therapeutics, Vitreogel may be used to treat other age-related macular diseases, such as diabetic macular edema and diabetic retinopathy. Its novel properties mean that it could even be used outside the medical field, in manufacturing and other industries.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">For now, however, one thing is clear. Vitreogel is set to bring about an exciting future for retinal detachment patients — one that is safer, more comfortable and brighter.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">This technology has been licensed to one company.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#ff0000;font-size:15px;font-family:'Playfair Display';">“I still remembered the moment when it gelled up, even though the process was in a matter of seconds, it felt like time stood still for a moment and I watched the liquid solution almost magically transform into a solid gel.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"><I>– Prof. Loh Xian Jun, Executive Director,</I></SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"><I>Institute of Materials Research and Engineering</I></SPAN></SPAN></DIV></div>

HTMLText_A820FA87_BC2B_B846_41C7_9857E5CF1845.html = <div style="text-align:left; color:#000; "><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:25px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"><B>Intelligent </B></SPAN><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';">Court</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:25px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';">Transcription System</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104681;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"><I>Singapore’s courtrooms zoom into the digital age with A*STAR’s Intelligent Court Transcription System, making real-time speech-to-text conversion of courtroom trials effortless.</I></SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Administrative processes for legal proceedings are arduous, but technology is helping to ease them. A*STAR’s Institute for Infocomm Research (I²R) has developed an artificial intelligence (AI)-powered transcription system that is now in use at the State Courts of Singapore.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The Intelligent Court Transcription System (iCTS) recognises and instantly transcribes human speech to text, allowing judges, prosecutors and defence counsel to review oral testimonies on the spot.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The evidence is clear: iCTS handles transcriptions with 90 per cent accuracy</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Dr. Tran Huy Dat and his team at I²R behind the iCTS project — including key project members Dr. Luong Trung Tuan and Mr. Tran Anh Dung — were inspired by the unique challenges of courtroom transcription.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“We set out to meet actual needs in the State Courts where the court reporter and transcribers spend long hours and take great effort to transcribe these court sessions after every court hearing,” explains Dr. Tran, who is Deputy Department Head of I²R’s Aural &amp; Language Intelligence Department.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">A normal courtroom proceeding transcription done manually typically takes betweenthree to seven days to complete as digitally recorded court proceedings are transcribed off-site by external service providers. The iCTS system, on the other hand, generates a quick draft of the court proceedings instantly, reducing the time needed for cross-checking by court writers thereafter.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Simultaneous transcription is also especially challenging given Singapore’s ethnic makeup. With the State Courts handling about 90 per cent of the overall caseload here, people who enter the courtroom come from all walks of life, with different accents and regular code-switching between languages and dialects.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The complexities of courtroom transcription makes iCTS all the more remarkable. Understanding speech in a court hearing requires a trained ear to navigate technical legal language, identify multiple speakers in cross-examinations, and distinguish between ambient sounds and cross talk. The iCTS outperforms other commercial speech-to-text solutions, scoring an error rate that is 25 to 30 per cent lower than the Google speech-to-text engine in a recent test. And its overall accuracy rate? An impressive 90 per cent.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Innovation in the first degree: Signal processing and speech-to-text engines that are made to measure</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The fact is that commercial AI assistants available today are not trained to operate smoothly in a Singapore courtroom environment. These AI systems are predominantly trained using data based on Western accents, manners of speech and cultural norms, and therefore function best in Western societies. Thus a large part of Dr. Tran’s work focused on customising the iCTS to meet the State Court’s unique needs.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">For instance, his team applied deep learning data augmentation, developing sound propagation models that automatically generate simulated variations of local accents and courtroom speech, to use as AI training data. Using these large data sets, the team trained the iCTS AI to process and transcribe local accents, dialects and slang, as well as court-specific lingo and domainspecificvocabulary, such as medical terms for coroner’s inquiries.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">To eliminate cross talk and boost transcription performance, Dr. Tran’s team leaned into their expertise in cutting-edge voice activity detection technology.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“Voice Activity Detection plays a crucially important role in the good performance of the system amid possible crosstalk effects, but it must be quick enough to be real-time. We intuitively applied an algorithm that won us the IARPA ASpIRE Challenge (Intelligence Advanced Research Projects Activity Automatic Speech Recognition in Reverberant Environments Challenge) and amazingly, it works well and saved us a lot of headaches,” Dr. Tran says.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">This award-winning engine helps iCTS accurately distinguish main speakers from noise. By concurrently measuring voice power, signal periodicity (i.e. how frequently a signal occurs) and coherence parameters (which allow relative examination of multiple data sets), it ensures that iCTS recognises and decodes voice and audio signals even in the presence of ambient noise and echoes.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">While technological challenges did not faze the team, a facilities upgrade did present a major challenge, he reveals.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">When the State Courts moved into its new building in 2021, the iCTS failed to perform accurately in initial tests because the algorithms were designed according to the acoustic conditions of the old courtrooms.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Thankfully, Dr. Tran’s team managed to resolve the problem with their expertise. “Luckily, after some acoustic fine-tuning sessions, the accuracy came back,” Dr. Tran shares with relief.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The verdict is out: Intelligent systems the way forward for Singapore’s nextgeneration courthouses</SPAN><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"> </SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">By equipping the State Courts with instantaneous transcription capabilities, Singapore’s judicial system is better prepared to meet the evolving needs of in-person and online court proceedings.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">For instance, judges, prosecutors and defence counsel in criminal hearings can now access recorded evidence immediately, which allows for more effective questioning of witnesses on the stand. When witnesses cannot be heard clearly or when speakers give unclear testimonies, such real-time transcripts can help parties intervene for clarification, therefore improving the effectiveness of cross-examination.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Whether in-session or out, court officers can also use the iCTS search function to locate specific parts of the evidence to seek clarification, helping to conduct cases more quickly and effectively. To top it off, its high degree of accuracy allows court officers and transcribers to engage inhigher-value verification work, accelerating court proceedings.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">For Dr. Tran’s team, the success of iCTS is just the beginning. I²R’s instantaneous and accurate localised transcription technology offers value to sectors such as media communications, archival services and education, and its innovation can be used for any high-level boardroom meeting. “Of course, we are very happy but also aware of new challenges ahead. There are talks on further collaborations with other agencies and we are ready to embrace these new challenges,” he says.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV></div>
