HTMLText_A9C1A501_BC2B_A83B_41DB_5CF042026184.html = <div style="text-align:left; color:#000; "><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:20px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:20px;font-family:'Gotham Rounded Medium';"><B>Co-axial Stereo Vision for 3D Wire Bond Inspection</B></SPAN></SPAN></DIV></div>
HTMLText_A9C8C505_BC2B_A83B_41DF_A1B4D3A95810.html = <div style="text-align:left; color:#000; "><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:25px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"><B>Respiree</B></SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104681;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"><I>A*STAR start-up Respiree is marrying the stethoscope and the smart watch to measure respiratory patterns in real time.</I></SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">What goes on in a COVID-19 isolation ward? Every four hours, healthcare workers in heavy personal protective gear enter each room. They measure the patients’ respiratory rate and oxygen saturation to determine if their condition has deteriorated. This process carries plenty of risks: what if the doctors and nurses are exposed to pathogens? What if the patient rapidly deteriorates sometime in between the four-hour interval?</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“If one were to visit most hospital general wards, the only vital sign still measured manually is the patient’s respiratory rate,” shares A*STAR senior research scientist, Dr. Gurpreet Singh. He was struck by how this crucial indicator of patients’ clinical status was monitored in such a cumbersome manner. “Respiratory rate is the vital sign that shows the earliest change in clinical status. Unfortunately, it is also the vital sign that is least measured in an automated manner in hospitals,” he says.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Now, picture this: instead of manual monitoring, crucial respiratory patterns are taken round-the-clock using a small wearable device: a sensor patch affixed on the chest. Just as a smart watch tracks our heart rate and step count, these devices measure vital markers like respiratory rate, breathing pattern variability and blood oxygen level. Healthcare workers can now access the smart devices’ data from dashboards outside the isolation wards. If there is any change in a patient’s status, doctors and nurses can respond in an instant.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"> </SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Breathing easy</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The company making this life-saving scenario possible is Respiree, a medical technology start-up founded in May 2019 and based on the work of Dr. Singh and his fellow scientists at A*STAR’s Singapore Bioimaging Consortium, now the Institute of Bioengineering and Bioimaging (IBB). By making patient monitoring automated and wearable, Respiree is re-imagining how we live with COVID-19 and other illnesses which could affect the respiratory system.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Respiree integrates cardio-respiratory detection and artificial intelligence to monitor and anticipate the condition of patients with respiratory diseases such as pneumonia and COVID-19, allowing for quick intervention by healthcare workers.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"> </SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">While the goal of predicting and preventing respiratory deteriorations seemed straight forward enough, the process of bringing Respiree to market was anything but easy. “Like all medical device companies, navigating the ecosystem is especially difficult and long,” says Dr. Singh.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Healthcare innovations such as Respiree have to go through long trials to ensure the efficacy and safety of the technology behind them. Thereafter, approval has to be given by regulatory bodies in each country. Medtech companies must carefully time their entire production pipeline so that their products can be validated, approved, produced and finally used commercially.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Despite this difficult process, within a year of its development, Respiree secured approval from Singapore’s Health Sciences Authority. Within two years, Respiree secured an international medical device regulatory approval by CE marking (under the Medical Device Directive). It is also working with local hospitals like Changi General Hospital and National University Hospital (NUH) to pilot and deploy Respiree.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Additionally, Respiree is working with both diagnostic and pharmaceutical companies to explore potential applications outside of healthcare settings.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">A breath of fresh air</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Launched in 2020, smack in the middle of the COVID-19 pandemic, Respiree’s potential applications in diagnosis and patient monitoring have created an urgent need for it. To tap on this potential, many projects involving the use of Respiree in hospitals are underway.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">One such project is the collaborative research study between Respiree, NUH and NUS Yong Loo Lin School of Medicine, which leverages Respiree to predict worsening conditions in isolated COVID-19 patients. Physicians can more easily measure patients’ vital data from the distanced safety of a dashboard outside the isolation wards, minimising infection risk. As new and more contagious COVID-19 variants continue to appear, the remote monitoring benefits of Respiree cannot be understated.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Yet, it’s not only patients in hospitals who stand to benefit from Respiree. Respiree could tell you when it is time to take a breather from work, or when you need to start making lifestyle changes for the better. As an unobtrusive blue patch, Respiree sensors can be worn on everyday clothing to measure your breathing and heart rates throughout the day. These patterns are analysed and displayed via an accompanying mobile app, providing insights on your stress levels and potential health conditions such as bronchitis or pneumonia.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Given both its clinical and personal applications, interest in Respiree extends far beyond Singapore. The platform is now awaiting approval from the USA Food and Drug Administration (FDA), and also being tested for deployment in several other countries including, Malaysia, Australia and Indonesia.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Despite the arduous process of commercialising Respiree, Dr. Singh and his team are heartened by the knowledge that their technology will save lives. The most pivotal moment for them was witnessing first-hand in a clinical setting how Respiree could provide early detection of patient deterioration. “It was truly the “seeing is believing moment” for us,” shares Dr. Singh.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“Perseverance pays off eventually. Medical device development is a marathon, not a sprint. Sustained endurance is key,” Dr. Singh says.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#ff0000;font-size:15px;font-family:'Playfair Display';">“Perseverance pays off eventually. In medical device development, it is a marathon not a sprint. Sustained endurance is key.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"><I>– Dr. Gurpreet Singh, Senior Research Scientist, Institute of Bioengineering and Bioimaging</I></SPAN></SPAN></DIV></div>
HTMLText_AF8324F0_BC2A_A9DA_41DB_D33F126E2F07.html = <div style="text-align:left; color:#000; "><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:20px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:20px;font-family:'Gotham Rounded Medium';"><B>Co-axial Stereo Vision for 3D Wire Bond Inspection</B></SPAN></SPAN></DIV></div>
HTMLText_AF83C4ED_BC2A_A9CA_41D2_41F81A80B8A5.html = <div style="text-align:left; color:#000; "><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:25px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"><B>Biomanufacturing Platform </B></SPAN><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';">for</SPAN><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"><B> Biologics Production</B></SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104681;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"><I>At A*STAR’s Bioprocessing Technology Institute, developing cell lines for biomanufacturing is no longer a needle-in-a-haystack search, thanks to a targeted integration platform that has shortened timelines from more than six months to less than nine weeks.</I></SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Since insulin was first isolated from canine pancreases in 1921, biologic drugs made from living organisms have been used to treat several diseases ranging from diabetes to cancer. Despite their diverse applications and effectiveness, biologics can be time- and labour-intensive to manufacture, raising costs and making treatment less affordable for patients.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">To manufacture biologics, cells — commonly derived from Chinese hamster ovaries (CHO) — are engineered via a gene transfer to produce therapeutic proteins such as antibodies. Due to technological limitations, this has traditionally been done through random integration. Transgenes carrying instructions for protein synthesis are introduced to a cell culture; these genes then integrate at random locations along cells’ DNA. This is done with the hope that at least one of the new recombinant cells will be a viable candidate as a production cell line. The late Prof. Miranda Yap, founding Executive Director of A*STAR’s Bioprocessing Technology Institute (BTI) had the foresight to initiate a research programme on CHO to bring Singapore to the forefront of biologics research.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Hundreds if not thousands of randomly engineered CHO cells must then be screened, one by one, for their ability to stably produce the desired protein and clone themselves for mass production. Most, however, do not. The process becomes even more complicated with the use of large cell cultures to increase the likelihood of a successful integration. To put it simply: narrowing the pool of cell line candidates is a major challenge in biomanufacturing, but expanding the pool provides greater odds of overall success. It’s this painstaking selection stage which creates months- to years-long “bottlenecks” in cell line development, according to Dr. Yang Yuansheng.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">At BTI, Dr. Yang, Lead Scientist for Cell Line Development, and his colleagues including Senior Lead Research Officer Ms. Jessna Yeo and Lead Research Officer Ms. Mariati, worked to develop cost-competitive cell lines for biomanufacturing.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“Over five years, we conducted hundreds of studies on traditional cell line development technologies to understand their limitations,” shares Dr. Yang. It quickly became apparent that targeted integration would be the solution to their problems.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The bumpy ride to smooth landings</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Targeted integration relies on the use of sitespecific recombinases, which are enzyme catalysts for DNA recombination. Site-specific recombinases only activate in the presence of a particular sequence in a host cell’s DNA, then act as a homing device or ‘landing pad’ for transgenes introduced into the host cell. These landing pads can be targeted to DNA sequences which are able to support prolific and stable protein production. When more than one site-specific recombinase is used, integration points can be triangulated even more precisely.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">If random integration is akin to a drifting message in a bottle, targeted integration is like an addressed package with tracking included. But first, Dr. Yang, Ms. Jessna Yeo, Ms. Mariati and the team would have to invent the postal service.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“The targeted integration was working and our production cycles had shortened, but the protein yield was still far below the industrial standard for biomanufacturing,” Dr. Yang recalls. Other labs worldwide were similarly unsuccessful, and there was growing scepticism over the commercial viability of targeted integration.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">BTI’s cell line development team took these obstacles in their stride “I tried to reframe our failures as prompts to relook and re-design research approaches,” Ms. Mariati reflects, “unexpected results can sometimes drive research even further”. A breakthrough moment eventually arrived, through the establishment of the second landing pad in CHO cells, and optimisation of the culture conditions in which successfully-engineered cells were isolated for multiplication. Although the figurative post office was finally open for business, this wasn’t the end of the team’s troubles.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“The biopharmaceutical industry is quite conservative, so finding industrial partners to validate our new technology was challenging,” said Dr. Yang. Fortunately, the BTI cell line development team found willing collaborators in Singapore’s biotech startup scene, Prestige BioPharma and Hummingbird Bioscience. Singapore-based Prestige BioPharma focuses on the development of biosimilars and new antibody therapeutics, and has successfully completed late-stage clinical trials on one of its biosimilars for breast and gastric cancer. Hummingbird Bioscience specialises in the development of novel antibodies against targets which have been elusive and difficult to drug, and has three flagship products currently at the clinical POC trials. The successful collaborations with these companies convinced larger international players to adopt the new cell line development platform.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Sticking the landing</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">BTI’s dual-landing pad, targeted integration cell line development platform has cut the average timeline for cell line development from over six months to under nine weeks. Lifesaving treatment drugs can be developed and commercialised faster than previously thought.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Additionally, the strategic targeting of DNA sequences has increased both the quality and stability of engineered cell lines, opening the doors to the production of more complex therapeutic proteins, such as bispecific antibodies.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Dr. Yang, a father of two, compares the research process to child-rearing: “You just have to roll with the punches and never give up”.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“Every research project is like an adventure. You never know what will happen,” says Ms. Mariati.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">This technology has been filed for one patent family and licensed to seven companies.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#ff0000;font-size:15px;font-family:'Playfair Display';">“Every research project is like an adventure. You never know what will happen.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"><I>– Ms. Mariati, Lead Research Officer, Bioprocessing Technology Institute</I></SPAN></SPAN></DIV></div>
HTMLText_AF8584BE_BC2A_A849_41BD_BF8E3D8F54E4.html = <div style="text-align:left; color:#000; "><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:25px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"><B>Auretek </B></SPAN><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';">Handheld Probe</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104681;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"><I>Scientists from A*STAR’s Institute of Bioengineering and Bioimaging can look under your skin with the world’s first handheld skin analyser.</I></SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Eczema is usually thought of as a skin disease — while not inaccurate, its effects on an individual reach beyond the superficial. The red, dry patches of skin on the insides of elbows and the backs of knees can cause so much prolonged pain that one’s self-confidence is undermined. In Singapore, 20 per cent of children and 11 per cent of adults suffer from eczema, making it one of the most common chronic conditions here.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Yet, existing medical tools to analyse and treat it are expensive, limited and difficult to use. Conventional skin analysers are large, benchtop apparatuses that cannot analyse all parts of the body, especially those harder-toreach locations. Hence, doctors have to rely on imprecise visual observations, hindering their ability to accurately diagnose and treat their patients.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">However, such diagnosis limitations could soon be a thing of the past. Auretek, an invention by A*STAR scientists in 2019, promises to radically transform the diagnosis process and consequently, the treatment of skin conditions.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Seeing skin clearly</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Between expensive surgery and the subjectivity of visual observation and diagnosis, the treatment process for skin conditions like eczema has always been less than ideal. After encountering the limitations of existing skin analysers, a team of scientists at A*STAR’s Institute of Bioengineering and Bioimaging (IBB) realised that they had the expertise to create something better.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“This device was invented for a purpose as I felt there was a urgent need to make a portable handheld device to screen patients with eczema as current existing technology used by doctors couldn’t provide this point-of-care testing for these patients,” says Professor Malini Olivo, Deputy Executive Director of IBB and Executive Director of A*STAR’s Health and MedTech Horizontal Technology Programme Office.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Their product, Auretek, is the first of its kind. It uses light technology and artificial intelligence to measure bio chemical components of the skin at different depths. Clinicians using Auretek can thus non-invasively analyse patients’ skin health beyond the surface, without having to perform a biopsy.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Most crucially, Auretek takes the form of a flexible, handheld probe. Gone are the days of visual examinations and clunky benchtop systems — Auretek allows dermatologists to finally pick up a skin analyser and bring it to the very spot troubling a patient.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">By the skin of their teeth</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Building the first-ever handheld skin analyser in the world was more difficult than the scientists had anticipated. Most benchtop analysers employ confocal Raman microscopy, which uses the interaction of light with the chemical bonds of molecules to identify skin components quickly and noninvasively. However, during the initial process of adapting the Raman microscopy system to work in a handheld probe, the scientists hit a roadblock. They found that when they tested the probe, there was a high level of “noise” — random fluctuations that hindered accurate measurement.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“In the beginning, we had no idea why there was such noise on top of the real signal. At least ten possible solutions were tested by us, but it still could not be solved,” recounts Prof. Malini.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Despite the disheartening results, the scientists persevered. After tedious experimentation and constant references to scientific theories, they hit a breakthrough. Realising that there was a problem with the detection method used by the probe, the team made tweaks to the measuring mechanism. Crisis was averted — the signal quality improved dramatically.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Other problems required external help. While the team wanted to create a small probe that could be easily handled, the standard optical components that they used for their prototype made it bulky and difficult to use. In order to miniaturise the probe, smaller optical components like lenses and filters would have to be custom-made. The small team was unequipped to manufacture such equipment, but they knew that others could do it.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Resourceful as ever, the team reached out to several local companies with optical-design expertise. Together, they created customised components that reduced the size of the probe considerably. “Currently, our latest probe is only about 20 per cent of the original size, which makes it very easy to use and quite flexible,” says Prof. Malini.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The story etched on our skin</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">With Auretek, dermatologists can precisely map our skin’s components using a cost-effective and user-friendly tool, giving them the ability to make more accurate diagnoses, give better prescriptions and monitor the efficiency of treatment more closely.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Even those without skin conditions can stand to benefit from the invention of Auretek. The probe can be used to test the skin’s reaction to ingredients in dermo-cosmetic products, such as skincare items, sunscreens and more.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Auretek, in other words, has a place beyond clinical use; it has the potential to make reverberations across the industry. This is something that gives the team at A*STAR immense satisfaction. Prof. Malini declares, “After we finished the benchmark testing against the standard commercial equipment and analysed the positive results, we felt that all the efforts were worthwhile.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">This technology has been filed for one patent family.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#ff0000;font-size:15px;font-family:'Playfair Display';">“This device was invented for a purpose as I felt there was a urgent need to make a portable handheld device to screen patients with eczema as current existing technology used by doctors couldn’t provide this point-of-care testing for these patients.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"><I>– Prof. Malini Olivo, Deputy Executive Director, Institute of Bioengineering and Bioimaging, and Executive Director, Health and MedTech Horizontal Technology Programme Office, A*STAR</I></SPAN></SPAN></DIV></div>

HTMLText_AF890513_BC2A_A85E_41E7_931D74E47407.html = <div style="text-align:left; color:#000; "><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:25px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"><B>Catalyst</B></SPAN><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"> for Converting</SPAN><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"><B> CO₂</B></SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:25px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104681;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"><I>A nickel catalyst developed by A*STAR’s Institute of Chemical and Engineering Sciences efficiently converts waste CO₂ into useful methane fuel.</I></SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">In their bid to fight climate change, governments and companies worldwide are now redoubling their carbon capture, utilisation and storage (CCUS) efforts. Baroque solutions — including a mechanical tree farm which absorbs carbon dioxide (CO₂) and fleets of empty balloons floating around Israel’s upper atmosphere — make the headlines intermittently. These and conventional CCUS efforts, though, capture mainly waste CO₂. And they do nothing with it after.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Researchers at A*STAR’s Institute of Chemical and Engineering Sciences (ICES) and their industry partner have found a better way to make use of waste CO₂ — by converting it to fuel.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Dr. Chen Luwei, Senior Scientist and Team Leader at ICES and her team, including project members Dr. Armando Borgna, Dr. Daniel Ong and Dr. Poh Chee Kok, have developed a nanostructured nickel-based catalyst, robust and efficient for industrial use, which converts CO₂ and hydrogen into methane. Methane produced in this manner is generally called substitute or synthetic natural gas (SNG). SNG has a potential and major industrial application as a storage medium for renewable energy such as hydrogen, owing to its ease of transport through existing gas pipes and infrastructure.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Nano nickel recalibrations</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">To make the industrial production of methane from waste CO₂ more efficient, a catalyst is needed. Catalysts react well with other materials on the molecular level, breaking bonds and forming new ones many times faster than when none are used.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Classically, nickel is an excellent, abundant and economical catalyst for the Sabatier reaction, which between 300 to 400 degrees Celsius turns CO₂ and hydrogen into methane and water.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Nickel is not perfect, though.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">It is susceptible to three undesirable factors, also known as carbon deposition, sulphur “poisoning” and sintering (clumping), which are the primary causes of eventual “death” or permanent deactivation of a catalyst.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Industrial catalysts are usually expected to last for years, as plant systems have to be interrupted whenever spent catalysts need to be replaced. Durability is therefore always a prized feature of good catalysts.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">To overcome nickel’s baggage of technical challenges as a material for catalysis, ICES collaborated with Japanese engineering firm IHI Corporation, which has established technologies in carbon capture and utilisation solutions; the novel catalyst was then unveiled in 2019. The catalyst developed by the ICES team is custom designed for IHI’s methanation reactor system to convert CO₂ to methane, and a demonstration unit of this system is housed in ICES on Jurong Island.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“Our catalyst has nickel nanoparticles fixed in place in a porous silica shell, like raisins spread within a muffin. This structure prevents the nickel nanoparticles from moving, thus averting sintering,” explains Dr Chen.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">This “nanomuffin” structure resulted in a durable catalyst that outperformed the benchmark commercial catalyst, with a lifespan twice as long.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The team was a full five floors up on an outdoor scaffolding at IHI’s Yokohama pilot plant when they were waiting for the moment of truth. It was a freezing cold morning filled with anticipation — but the test results were elusive.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“We had two test tubes,” recalls Dr. Chen. “One had our catalyst and the other had a benchmark catalyst.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The difference between those two, however, was not noticeable at the end of the first day.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“Although we were quite confident that our catalyst should be better, we were still nervous,” says Dr. Chen, “After a long anxious wait, the difference became obvious on the second day. The exciting moment finally came, and a cheer went up from every member at the site. Our catalyst beat the benchmark at the field test in the end.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Slowing Down Climate Change</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Well-designed and cost-efficient catalysts like this one jointly developed by ICES and IHI may mean the accelerated realisation of a sustainable future where CO₂ emissions no longer rise into the atmosphere, but are instead harnessed and turned into a useful resource.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Perhaps, then, this catalyst is a timely intervention in our era of climate change.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">This technology has been filed for two patent families.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#ff0000;font-size:15px;font-family:'Playfair Display';">“After a long anxious wait, the difference became obvious on the second day. The exciting moment finally came and a cheer went up from every member at the site. Our catalyst beat the benchmark at the field test in the end.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"><I>– Dr. Chen Luwei, Senior Scientist and Team Leader, Institute of Chemical and Engineering Sciences</I></SPAN></SPAN></DIV></div>

While existing systems often classify emotions into crude categories (positive or negative, happy or unhappy, angry or calm), CrystalFeel — which recognises both English and localised Singlish expressions — breaks down emotions across multiple dimensions.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">For example, in a status post like “What do I do with my life … I have no more choices …”, CrystalFeel recognises intense sadness and fear, even though these emotions are expressed in the linguistic context without using any strong emotional words such as “desperate” or “hopeless”. Digital Emotions’ multimodal, multilingual capabilities has enabled organisations to innovate in media analytics, consumer care, hospitality and even recruitment services, making them more relevant to our diverse ethnic makeup.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">To top it all off, Dr. Yang’s team has integrated their technologies for a more seamless usage experience. Built around the capabilities of Crystalace, CrystalFeel and A*Digital Emotions, Heartbeat is a social and news analysis platform offering real-time trend visualisation for R&amp;D use, while Resonance Social is an industry-strength system that collects, analyses and presents end-to-end social media data in user-friendly dashboards with customisable keyword search capabilities. This makes it easy for anyone — even tech newbies — to access and use A*STAR’s social analytics technologies. This seamless social listening solution has provided timely data which have aided the understanding of public sentiments and emotional responses to the COVID-19 pandemic.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Heightened spidey senses: Digital emotions analysis offers users both descriptive insights and predictive capabilities </SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Given that A*STAR’s inventors are tech-nological pioneers, it is no surprise that their innovations perform amongst the best in its class.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Benchmarked against three commercially available emotion analysis solutions (including IBM Watson’s Natural Language Understanding service), A*STAR’s digital emotion and sentiment technologies scored top marks in recent tests. HTMLText_AFA42597_BC2A_A846_41BF_F083AD3F6438.html = <div style="text-align:left; color:#000; "><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:25px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"><B>ETC-159 </B></SPAN><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';">Targets</SPAN><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"><B> Drug-</B></SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:25px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block;
