white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104681;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"><I>Drug-resistant cancers might become a thing of the past as Duke-NUS and A*STAR’s newest porcupine inhibitor ETC-159 joins the fight against the deadly disease.</I></SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Cancer looms large as one of the world’s most lethal diseases, claiming almost 10 million lives annually and accounting for roughly one in six deaths. It is both a nightmare for sufferers to experience and for their loved ones to behold. The proliferation of cancerous cells disrupts vital physiological processes and progressively overwhelms the body. In a worst-case scenario, certain cancer types can become drug-resistant, rendering them virtually untreatable.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Fortunately, the advent of porcupine inhibitors, also known as PORCNi, could give patients with dire prognoses a fighting chance.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Not all cancers are the same</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Hollywood might have you thinking that cancer treatments are limited to chemotherapy and radiotherapy but in reality, modern medicine is steering away from the scorched-earth tactics of traditional cancer treatments which come with destructive side effects.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Instead, researchers are increasingly looking into drugs that discern between malignant and healthy cells. Today, drugs such as anti PD-1 antibodies are used to harness the body’s own immune cells to kill cancer cells. Other drugs, such as poly adenosine diphosphate-ribosepolymerase (PARP) inhibitors, are used to prevent cancer cells from harnessing their natural ability to repair their own DNA. When the damage in the DNA accumulates, the cancer cells will die.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Unfortunately, some cancers have developed features that make them immune to such drugs. Subsets of colorectal, endometrial, pancreatic and ovarian cancers currently cannot be treated with PD-1 antibodies as they have hyperactive Wnt signalling pathways and few immune cells within the tumours. Some other cancers cannot be treated with PARP inhibitors due to hyperactive Wnt pathway that triggers DNA repair genes, allowing the cancer cells to supersede PARP inhibitors’ ability to prevent DNA repairs, and ultimately rendering PARP inhibitors ineffective.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Pricking cancer cells like a porcupine Unintimidated by the tenacity of the disease, Professor David Virshup, Director of the Programme in Cancer and Stem Cell Biology (CSCB) and Professor at Duke-NUS Medical School approached A*STAR with the idea of developing a PORCNi.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Porcupine inhibitors are emerging as a new hope against drug-resistant cancers. Researchers at A*STAR and Duke-NUS believe that Singapore’s very own ETC-159 is the best PORCNi compound developed to date.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Like other PORCNi drugs, ETC-159 is designed to inhibit PORCN, a protein-coding gene that regulates the Wnt pathway. However, in some cancers, it also increases the immune cells in the tumours allowing PD-1 inhibitors to work, while in others, it halts the production of PARP, shutting off the Wnt pathway and thus allowing cancer cells to die.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“While PORCNi drugs may have significant clinical potential, there has been no definitive clinical validation to date,” explains ETC-159 Asset Development Leader Dr. Veronica Diermayr at A*STAR’s Experimental Drug Development Centre (EDDC), “So, the race is still on amongst different developers to confirm PORCNi’s clinical utility.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">In 2015, ETC-159 entered its first-in-human clinical trial. Compared to conventional cancer treatments such as radiotherapy and chemotherapy, ETC-159’s side effects appear limited mainly to fatigue and anorexia.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">ETC-159 will achieve another milestone at the end of 2021 in its Phase 1B expansion trial. This will mark a monumental step forward as researchers will now focus on the efficacy of the drug and assess its safety as a treatment option.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Patients with microsatellite stable colorectal, endometrial or ovarian cancers will be given ETC-159 in hopes of treating their illness. The drug’s ability to slow or halt the growth of cancer cells in cancers with elevated Wnt signalling will be put to the test along with its ability to improve the activity of immunotherapy (PD-1 inhibitors) in this subset of patients who are typically unresponsive to this treatment.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Dr. Diermayr’s team members at EDDC, Dr. Thomas Keller, Senior Advisor, Chemistry, and Dr. Ho Soo Yei, the Lead Medicinal Chemist for ETC-159, are elated with the drug’s progress: “This signals that we can compete with international pharma and biotech companies which have also worked on porcupine inhibitors”. They caution, however, that “this is just the first step on the long road to registration”.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#104861;font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">A new lease of life</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">If successfully commercialised, ETC-159 could save countless lives worldwide. Globally, in 2020, almost 10.6 per cent of males and 9.4 per cent of females had colorectal cancer, which tends to have a high level of Wnt signalling and is non-responsive to immunotherapy treatments such as pembrolizumab. The science behind ETC-159’s development could also contribute to the development of new treatments for a broader range of cancer types.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">To get there, far more trial and error awaits the research team, but according to Dr. Keller and Dr. Ho, they are more than ready to rise to the occasion: “Drug discovery is a process that has many ups and downs. However, knowing when to stay the course is the secret ingredient for success.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="color:#ff0000;font-size:15px;font-family:'Playfair Display';">“Drug discovery is a process that has many ups and downs. However, knowing when to stay the course is the secret ingredient for success.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';"><I>– Dr. Thomas Keller, Senior Advisor, Chemistry, and Dr. Ho Soo Yei, Lead Medicinal Chemist,Experimental Drug Development Centre</I></SPAN></SPAN></DIV></div>

HTMLText_F3B58E84_E9F1_1CA7_41D3_D28DD28A2243.html = <div style="text-align:left; color:#000; "><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Gotham Rounded Medium';">In the early years, the importance of research and development (R&amp;D) was recognised and supported by continuous and strategic investments in key areas of research excellence. In early 1991, the National Science and Technology Board (NSTB), preceded by the Science Council, was established and tasked to formulate the long-term R&amp;D strategy and execute the plans to lay foundations, build infrastructure, galvanise resources and develop human capital for national growth.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Gotham Rounded Medium';">After a decade of phenomenal pioneering work, the Board evolved into the Agency for Science, Technology and Research (A*STAR) in early 2002. In this era, a range of research fields in physical, natural and engineering sciences, together with life sciences, was grown and elevated. A number of these emerged as top scientific fields in Singapore and the world, today. They also fuelled the capability and manpower needs of Singapore’s key economic pillars: manufacturing, pharmaceuticals, electronics, chemicals, biotechnology, data science and so forth. </SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Gotham Rounded Medium';">It was also during this period that the A*STAR Scholarship was launched and progressively expanded to focus on scientific talent as a key resource for Singapore, resulting in a core talent pool that galvanises R&amp;D efforts in Singapore.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Gotham Rounded Medium';"><B><I>Professor Andy Hor,</I></B></SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Gotham Rounded Medium';"><B><I>Deputy Chief Executive (Research), A*STAR</I></B></SPAN></SPAN></DIV></div>
HTMLText_F58ECBD3_E9F1_E4A1_41DA_5BB22E2A30B5.html = <div style="text-align:left; color:#000; "><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Gotham Rounded Medium';">It is evident that the outcomes of research are not merely measured by research outputs (viz. publications, patents…) but very importantly, the impact they have on science, technology, economy, society – in short, our livelihood and life. The pursuit of meaningful, impactful outcomes is driving research convergence in which R&amp;D is not simply multi-disciplinary but trans-disciplinary.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Gotham Rounded Medium';">To take on the challenges of sustainability, climate change, digitisation, healthcare, and advanced manufacturing, A*STAR’s broader research agenda must be recast, incorporating cross-boundary research disciplines to deliver solutions through innovative science. HTMLText_F5E64DA9_E9F1_1CE0_41CB_92E20C679896.html = <div style="text-align:left; color:#000; "><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Gotham Rounded Medium';">Faster Tests, Automated Systems and Reusable Masks: How A*STAR and Singapore Held the Line against COVID-19</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Gotham Rounded Medium';">23 January 2020. At that moment, our lives, as we know it, changed irrevocably. Cases rose exponentially in the following months, no thanks to the highly contagious nature of the virus. </SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Gotham Rounded Medium';">In March 2020, 600 people were infected with COVID-19; one month later, the number exploded exponentially and hit 15,000.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Gotham Rounded Medium';">This figure seems shocking — but on hindsight, it is likely that it could have been a lot higher, had Singapore and the collective research ecosystem not banded together to help control the spread of the virus; A*STAR researchers stepped up to the plate.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV></div>

HTMLText_F7F54A24_E9F1_E7E0_41E2_207BD600AFE8.html = <div style="text-align:left; color:#000; "><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Gotham Rounded Medium';">In the aftermath of the 2007 to 2008 global financial crisis, the emphasis on business innovation as well as translation and commercialisation of R&amp;D prompted A*STAR to foster open innovation through a myriad of public-private partnership and collaborative programmes with the industry. It set the journey to venture from research to enterprise through innovation. It also laid the cornerstone of the knowledge-based economy that Singapore strives to develop.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Gotham Rounded Medium';">These cross-organisational and transboundary collaborations resulted in the explosive growth of Intellectual Property (IP) in the form of patents, licenses and know-how, and developed the expertise needed to support industry growth, both in multinational and local enterprises. A selected few of the inventions and innovations are highlighted in this publication. HTMLText_F844B6ED_BC3E_69CB_41D7_4A946FE8F82F.html = <div style="text-align:left; color:#000; "><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:25px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"><B>Fortitude</B></SPAN><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';">: Singapore’s</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:25px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';">first COVID-19 </SPAN><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"><B>diagnostic test</B></SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Back when COVID-19 was still called “2019-nCoV”, Tan Tock Seng Hospital’s (TTSH) Department of Laboratory Medicine was already developing a COVID-19 test kit in partnership with A*STAR’s Bioinformatics Institute (BII) and Experimental Drug Development Centre (EDDC).</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The team, comprising scientists like Dr. Sebastian Maurer-Stroh from BII, Dr. Masafumi Inoue from EDDC, Dr. Timothy Barkham from TTSH and Dr. Sidney Yee from the Diagnostics and Development (DxD) Hub, managed to speed through the design, development, production and deployment of the new diagnostic test.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">It started in January 2020 when Dr. MaurerStroh began to examine the genomic sequence of the virus, which had been uploaded to the Global Initiative on Sharing all Influenza Data (GISAID) database by scientists in China. After poring over the data, he shared the information with Dr. Inoue who then used the sequence to design the test.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Known as a detection primer, it is a short strand of DNA that when used in PCR can target and duplicate specific DNA segments. “It took only 48 hours to design detection primers for the novel coronavirus from the time complete sequences were published,” says Dr Inoue.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The next step was for Dr. Barkham to refine and evaluate the test using real clinical samples from the hospital. The baton was then passed to DxD Hub, where Dr. Weng Ruifen, Chief Technology Officer of DxD Hub, led the design, development, production and onboarding of the kit, as well as the technology transfer of the production and onboarding expertise to local biotech firm MiRXES.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Named the Fortitude SARS-CoV-2 Kit, the diagnostic test was successfully completed in January 2020 — the very month Dr. Maurer-Stroh started looking at the coronavirus’s genome.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The Fortitude Kit is a one-step Reverse Transcription-Polymerase Chain Reaction (RT-PCR) test. Simply put, PCR technology increases the amount of genetic material gathered from the tiny amount swabbed from your nasopharynx such that the presence of the coronavirus can be confirmed via special laboratory equipment. Instead of finding a needle in a haystack, PCR technology has narrowed the search to finding a needle in your sewing kit.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The Fortitude Kit came with pre-mixed reagents as well as quality-control tubes, minimising the chances for human error and cutting down on diagnosis time by about 30 per cent compared to testing without the use of any diagnostic kit.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The kit has proved so efficient and accurate that it is in routine use in 13 Singapore hospitals and labs, both public and private. It is also deployed in over 20 countries worldwide, including New Zealand, the United States and Indonesia.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">DxD Hub and TTSH went on to expand the Fortitude Kit’s diagnostic capability and made it possible to test for both COVID-19 and influenza A and B at the same time, since patients infected with either virus exhibit similar symptoms.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV></div>

HTMLText_F84656F4_BC3E_69DA_41DC_C83860C030BE.html = <div style="text-align:left; color:#000; "><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:25px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"><B>RAVE: </B></SPAN><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';">Automation boosts</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:25px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">One of the cornerstones of effective management of the pandemic is a good testing regime, and diagnostics capabilities to support it.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The need for a better COVID-19 diagnostics solution became acute when cases started to rise in Singapore during the early phase of the pandemic.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Lab operators were taking turns working day and night to process the rising numbers of clinical samples entering their labs, with no end in sight.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“You can imagine that there was a lot of operator fatigue, and that is a problem for diagnostic assays because when the operators are tired, there will be errors in the assay set-up and that will result in mistakes in the test reports,” says Dr. Weng.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Fortunately, a collaboration between biologists from DxD Hub and engineers from the Advanced Remanufacturing and Technology Centre (ARTC) and the Singapore Institute of Manufacturing Technology (SIMTech) gave rise to the ultimate solution.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Known as the Rapid Automated Volume Enhancer (RAVE), the robotics lab system cuts down the manual steps involved in the preparation of a test assay, such as unscrewing tubes and pipetting. RAVE is designed to work with the RESOLUTE 2.0 kits, and each unit is able to handle a throughput of around 4,000 samples a day.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Recounting the short and accelerated development process, Mr. Victor Chan, Senior Project Manager at ARTC and SIMTech, and Programme Manager for A*STAR’s COVID-19 Solutions Programme, said, “We started to work with the scientists at GIS and DxD Hub to understand the workflow, and from there we found parts of the process where automation could have the largest impact. The development of RAVE has shown that automation can add huge value to diagnostics testing. And A*STAR together with our SME system integrators definitely have the capabilities to play in this field.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Aside from boosting the nation’s COVID-19 testing capabilities, one of the greatest benefits of RAVE was the enhanced safety it brought to lab operators through automation.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV></div>
HTMLText_F84756FC_BC3E_69CA_41E7_BC47438C5964.html = <div style="text-align:left; color:#000; "><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:25px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"><B>RESOLUTE 2.0: First multiplex</B></SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:25px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"><B>direct PCR </B></SPAN><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';">assay approved by</SPAN><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"><B> HSA</B></SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Diversity is strength, and that applies to diagnostic kits as well.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">In the face of a global supply chain heavily impacted by COVID-19, DxD Hub and DSO National Laboratories (Singapore’s national defence research organisation) co-developed the breakthrough Direct-PCR diagnostic test kit for COVID-19, RESOLUTE 2.0. Built on a molecular-based assay co-developed and productized by DSO and DxD Hub, it was launched in July 2020 to complement other diagnostics options available in the market. Singapore-based company Advanced MedTech Holdings took on the manufacturing and distribution of the kit.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">RESOLUTE2.0 is a direct-PCR test that eliminates the need for the extraction of viral RNA from patient test samples, thereby minimising potential human errors and shortening the time required to complete the test. It comes with two reagents – a marked improvement from the original version developed in early 2020 which had 14. This simplification of the kit makes it much faster to set up the assays. More importantly, as the RESOLUTE 2.0 is an extraction-free PCR solution, the breakthrough development alleviates the dependance on nucleic acid extraction reagent kits (which are needed with conventional PCR tests), the global shortage of which became a bottleneck to COVID-19 PCR testing in Singapore and many other countries in 2020.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The kit was in development when Singapore implemented its circuit breaker period and the heightened restrictions that followed. All hands were needed on deck, but the pandemic situation made it highly risky for all staff to continue working on the kit at the same time.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“We decided to really bite the bullet and work around the clock, and that meant we had to work in shifts that would allow us to maintain full capacity,” recalled Dr. Sidney Yee, Chief Executive Officer at DxD Hub. “That was very challenging and trying, yet really a motivating moment for our team to really decide that we’re just going to do this no matter what.” </SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Most people who have undergone a PCR swab test would agree that it is an unpleasant experience. Since late 2020, DxD Hub and DSO have developed a RESOLUTE 2.0 kit that works with deep-throat saliva samples and can be self-administered, bypassing the painful and invasive nasopharyngeal swabbing process.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Looking back on the journey for RESOLUTE 2.0, Dr. Weng shared the recipe for the successful product development: “There are three ingredients – great public-private partnership, an awesome team who share a common goal, and good perseverance when we encounter challenges.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV></div>
HTMLText_F84796EF_BC3E_69C7_41D2_4418B8C242A4.html = <div style="text-align:left; color:#000; "><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:20px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:20px;font-family:'Gotham Rounded Medium';"><B>Co-axial Stereo Vision for 3D Wire Bond Inspection</B></SPAN></SPAN></DIV></div>
HTMLText_F84DB6E6_BC3E_69F9_41D1_EF35BBF7284C.html = <div style="text-align:left; color:#000; "><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:20px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:20px;font-family:'Gotham Rounded Medium';"><B>Co-axial Stereo Vision for 3D Wire Bond Inspection</B></SPAN></SPAN></DIV></div>
HTMLText_F85AC703_BC3E_683E_41D7_DBBDA9E5968E.html = <div style="text-align:left; color:#000; "><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:25px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"><B>Unmasking</B></SPAN><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"> the science behind </SPAN><SPAN STYLE="font-size:25px;font-family:'Playfair Display';"><B>masks</B></SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">In the weeks that followed after the world learned that face masks would help reduce our risk of getting infected with COVID-19, panic buying ensued and mask-production lines struggled to keep up with the demand.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">At that time, Dr. Chng Shuyun, Acting Group Manager, Sustainable and Circular Process Technology Group, Mr. Lok Boon Keng, Group Manager, Printed Intelligence Device Group, and their teams at SIMTech and ARTC, in partnership with local textile manufacturer Ramatex, were hard at work to develop a face mask that was both reusable and provided excellent protection.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“While it was important to get people to mask up to prevent spread of the COVID-19 and save lives, the surge and the use of disposal masks could lead to a growing environmental problem when they end up in landfills, waterways and the ocean,” says Dr. Chng, “therefore, the team was looking to make a reusable version of the protective mask, as a more environmentally friendly option.”</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Supported by A*STAR’s scientific research, Ramatex produced a three-layer mask, each serving a unique line of defence against the virus. The synthetic innermost layer efficiently absorbs saliva while the outermost layer is highly repellant so that environmental droplets are kept away from the wearer.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">The highlight of the mask is its middle layer, which serves as a filter. When new, it has a bacterial filtration efficiency (BFE) of 98.5 per cent, which means that the filter can block 98.5 per cent of droplets about 3 microns in size. (For context, our cough droplets typically range from 5 to 20 microns, while a human hair, at 70 to 100 microns, is gigantic in comparison.)</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">As the filter layer is sandwiched — and hence protected — by the two other layers, the mask can withstand repeated washing without losing its BFE. Even after 30 washes, researchers found that the mask’s BFE remains close to 95 per cent, making it comparable to disposable, one-time-use surgical masks.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">Comfort was not sacrificed for safety and sustainability — the team factored in a “duck beak” design to ensure breathability. Indeed, the mask proved so effective and comfortable that it was the mask of choice to be included in 2020’s National Day Parade Fun Pack.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">“It was THE moment for us when we saw many people wearing the mask during the National Day Parade. That made the team and me really proud with an overwhelming sense of pride and satisfaction, and knowing we had really met the goal we set out to achieve – a reusable mask for the people,” recalled Mr. Lok.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV><p STYLE="margin:0; line-height:15px;"><BR STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-size:12px;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"/></p><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">More impressively, the team completed the development in a mere three months. More than 900,000 masks were manufactured by May 2020 so that students could return to schools safely; a further 7 million were produced in the following months, filling the gap in demand. To ensure that everyone had access to the masks, the team collaborated with Temasek Foundation to distribute the </SPAN></SPAN></DIV><DIV STYLE="text-align:left;font-size:15px;"><SPAN STYLE="display:inline-block; letter-spacing:0px; white-space:pre-wrap;color:#000000;font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><SPAN STYLE="font-size:15px;font-family:'Open Sans';">masks to all Singapore residents via self-service vendingmachines in the community.</SPAN></SPAN></DIV></div>
